O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the last of the art of medicine together with its contents, and I have finished it through its explanations and through its statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with the treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and has been lost from all to all, so the science has perished and has been scattered, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed off, and the science is removed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I will revitalize it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools of the craft along with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation for use, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to be well-versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he knows the joints of the members, and their forms, and their connections, and their separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and vessels, and the number of them, and their arrangement, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason says Hippocrates that a name with a name is much, but with the work it is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Now we say in the introduction to this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, should be careful lest he fall into error and harm people; thus I have warned many times those who undertake this science and abandon it without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut off the suppurative abscess or tumor from a woman's neck and cut through the arteries of the neck; why, so much blood came out that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I have seen another surgeon who treated a stone in an elderly man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he carried off with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he was operated on, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I have seen another surgeon who undertook to treat a duke of our land who had a broken leg and an open wound on it; and the ignorant surgeon fastened the splinter up over the wound with very tight bandages, and did not leave the wound any room for drainage, and thus left it in that condition. He commanded that the bandages should not be removed, and he remained in this way until the leg was entirely gangrened and the foot came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and free the leg; and when I had it loosed, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But despite my efforts to treat him, the corruption had already been confirmed in the member and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease its progress through the member until the entire member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I have seen another surgeon who abscessed a cancerous tumor, and then inflamed it with malicious intent.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	When the chancre is pure of melancholic humor, it does not seem necessary to touch it with iron unless it is in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, my dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, an operation in which there is danger in many situations; and I will show you in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Why it is necessary that you take care of yourselves so that foolish men cannot speak ill of you If you take up arms in season, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised; and leave frightening diseases with poor health; and put down your arms from those things that make you doubt, and be courageous in yourselves so that you can come into this world into the other world of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Gauls say in some of their warnings: "Do not undertake to treat a bad disease, lest you be called foolish physicians.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have written this book according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauterizing with fire and medical cauterization, and it is arranged from head to toe; and about the forms of the instruments, and the fixings of a cauterizer, and everything that is necessary in the operation.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and venesection (bloodletting), and wounds, and the extraction of splinters, and similar things; and it is arranged with the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to toe, with the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	And so that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to say what quality of aid and harm each temperament (or constitution) does.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest and most subtle science and secret answer; and many wise men have spoken about it and agreed on this; and I suffice with my words, because I fear the length. (Translation note: The sentence has a somewhat defensive tone, as if the author is anticipating criticism for not providing more detail.)
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterizing aids universally to all temperaments as long as there is matter, except for two temperaments: that is to say, the hot temperament with plenty of matter, and the dry temperament with plenty of matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry temperament together with plenty of matter, some said that cauterizing is a great aid, while others said the opposite: that cauterizing is not useful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be cured with heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite say that cauterizing makes great aid for hot and dry diseases that come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man to its moisture in the temperament of fire, you find the body cold. (This sentence suggests that despite being classified as a hot temperament, the body itself is actually cooler than expected, which could be relevant for cauterizing treatments.)
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, only he who has experienced it should intervene, and who knows the rules of cauterization through long practice, and the diversity of human temperaments, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the remedies and the timing; we have no fear of other temperaments, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the surgeons gathered together and agreed on cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cauterizing with fire is together a secret of good remedies, and of greater virtue than burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come except to the cooked member, and it harms no other member if one knows how.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The hot medicines come from member to member by removing [the excess], and cause the affected member to have poor health; and perchance kill the patient The fires because of their highness and the goodness of their substance do not make those things, if there is no surplus.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this for you by experiment and through the length of my service and study in this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of this speech, because I do not want to deprive you of the secret which is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says when demonstrating it. Accept it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done, and they chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is advisable in all times, because the subsequent harmings are put under by the help of cauterization; and similarly if the cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish surgeons do; for the disease that is cured by cauterization does not recur; and they say so themselves. But it's not true what they believe, because cauterizations are nothing but a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries out the humors that cause the pain, and surpasses other medicines in its haste, virtue of work, and dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it's possible that the disease will return at some time according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its virtue; and they are assembled within him the superfluities by the accumulation of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered in the place where there is an abundance of superfluities and moisture, as with dense cauters for pain, and similar things. And that kind of pain does not return, but this can happen.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and that's true; but they don't believe that cauterizations are worth it after other treatments, but their intention is false. And cauterizations are the last resort of medicine because when we administer other methods of treatment in some disease and they do not work, then we administer the cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterizations are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish surgeons.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizations made with a golden instrument are more effective than those made with iron, and they did not say this simply because of the fire, but rather because of the quality of gold and its high substance. And they said that the place where the cauterization is applied does not make a boil, but it's not true, for I have tried it and found that it is true in some people; and golden cauterizations are more effective than iron ones, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And nonetheless, when you heat an instrument of gold, you can't tell if it's hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down at once. And if you heat it too much, it melts in the fire; and thus there is quite enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because of that, we use iron cauterizations which are better suited to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter in the correct order from start to finish up to the end, so that the reading may be more easy to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauterizations are worth it for moisture and coldness on the head, and there are two that one makes because of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the head to the temples, and to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pains in the teeth and pain in the throat, and similarly for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that the patient be purged by a solvent medicine, clarifying the head, three or four times, as the virtues and age and habit of the patient can tolerate; and then make the head of the patient cool again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on the scale; afterwards put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and let the vein that comes in from the middle go, if it bleeds afterwards, heat the cauterization called "olive oil", which is the form.
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and move your hand down and outwards, little by little, turning as you go; then lift your hand suddenly, and reward the area if you see bone 1 small coin in size; and if you don't see it, repeat the cauterization until you see bone, just as I told you. Afterwards take 1 spoonful of silk thread, wet it with moist cotton inside, and place it on the spot, and leave it for 3 days. Then put on a damp linen bandage in butter; and let it stay there until the heat is gone. Afterwards treat the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacium" until it's healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancient ones said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges, and because of this, they considered it a great help.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that the cauterization should be applied so long that part of the bone is burned, and then take out what has been burned from the bone, and it will heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the cauterization should be applied so long and strongly that it reaches down to the bone as wide as a thread that women put in their looms, so that the humors can flow out freely; and the wound must remain open for a long time. Afterwards, it must be healed and dried up.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And I think that these two methods of cauterization are not entirely good in every case, except for those who are already weakened by some other illness. And it seems to me that I should leave them alone, because the nerves are weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we see in other parts of the body; and similarly, when the patient's nerves are weak by nature, and the first sign of cauterization is more severe and painful for me, and from this experience I have learned to avoid it.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	The ancient head pain (or headache)
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When a chronic pain comes to the head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use juices and pills called "cochie", and purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if one makes him the cauterization that we mentioned earlier, it is not worth it.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take heed if the patient's nerves are strong in nature and not too cold; then cauterize beneath that cauterization a spoonful of what we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards make a cauterization on each horn of the head up to the bone, just as we said before, and make one cauterization at the spot called "vasselz"; and it is one place where you put cupping glasses. And hold your hand so that you don't see up to the bone: the patient feels a much greater pain in this cauterization than in the others, and I will speak of this elsewhere; and it is necessary that the horn cauterizations be more subtle than those used for the middle part of the head, and this is the form.
dou cautere dou chief	The cauterization of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When a sudden pain comes to a part of the head and the disease spreads up to the eye, and the nerves are purged by clarifying medicines, and all the other treatments that I mentioned in the division of diseases have not helped: then one makes cauterizations according to two methods, namely with medicinal iron and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with medicinal iron is that you take a dose of alum, and peel off the rind and scrape it into a spoonful as two nerves, and then make an incision in the temple where the pain is, in such a way that you can put the alum paste under the skin. And when it has been put there, tie it tightly and leave it for 12 hours; and then untie it and treat further with alum paste, and let the wound be like this for 2 or 3 days, then apply a poultice in butter as long as the scabbing is still going on.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	Afterwards, treat with ointment until it is healed; and if you see fit to do any of the purging medicines that I have written about in my treatment of purging medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery so is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery until it reaches this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a key or it has a small lump of horn in the middle, and apply it to the painful spot; and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly so that the half of the thickness of the horn is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery doesn't burn, which is usually deeper, and bleed abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, put cotton soaked in silk thread on the spot and leave it for 3 days; then I put cotton moistened in butter, and treat the area with ointment until it is healed. And if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cauterizer called "cultellare", at the tip, and be careful not to touch the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	Migraine (or headache)
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauterizations mentioned earlier with medicine and fire do not work, then it is necessary to heat the cauterizer called "cultellare" until it is white; and mark a line with half a finger's length on the painful spot, and take your hand once, and strain so that you don't touch the artery and go up to the bone. Be careful of the mandible that moves when eating, and the nerves that have regard for it, and that spasms may come to the patient, and be careful of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear in the patient who does not know what it is, and who is not experienced; and leave the work in my way, but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it appears in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cauterization does not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, then cauterize on the inside of the head just as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you need to, administer the cauterizer that we mentioned in the chapter on extraction of the artery, with the cauterizer that has two blades; and this cauterization is better than the other one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of ear pain due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear due to coldness, and you have tried medicines that dissolve and other treatments that we mentioned in the division, and the pain does not change: then heat this cauterizer called "poins", which is in the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, prick all around the sick ear, or around both ears where the pain is felt in both, and pull away a little above the root of the ear as soon as you have marked the spot to be cauterized; and there should be 10 pricks around each ear. Then, cure the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth (or toothache)
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	The torture that should be treated with cauterization is not excepting those that are caused by wind, such as we mentioned in the division of diseases; and do not make a cauterization for symptoms that come from heat and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this symptom of torture that is caused by wind from the mouth and purging of the head and gargling, and it does not help: then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, and another a little deeper than the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and put the cauterizer in the part that appears healthy, and make a cauterization near the crown of the head above a little of the bone, and another in the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cauterizer so high up that half of the thickness of the horn is burned. This is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the form of the cultellare that we mentioned before, but it is a bit more subtle and it is necessary that the blades be a little thicker; afterwards, cure the wound just as I mentioned before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in the way we mentioned before, and it does not help, and the patient has no fever: then make four cauterizations: two on the two horns of the head, and one inside the head, and one at the spot called "vasselz" as we mentioned before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and cure it in the way we mentioned before.
de litargie	Of lethargy (or a state of being drowsy or listless)
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	To this disease it is necessary to give the patient large doses of juices and purifying pills for the brain; afterwards, make a head bath on the sick person, and put the sinapi plaster on the back of the head, which is written in the treatise on plasters. And this is the manner of cauterization: do it as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, then make three cauterizations inside the head going down to the neck, with a space of one finger between each cauterization as large as two fingers thick; and cure them just like the others. And if you see fit to add to them, and the patient is suffering, then make an additional cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two horns, and cure it until it is healed. This is the manner of the "olivare" cauterizer, as I mentioned before.
de la froidor dou chief	Of coldness of the head (or headaches caused by cold)
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with juices and what we mentioned before; afterwards, make a head bath on the sick person, then make cauterizations inside the head and on each horn, and one at the back of the neck and three on the spine of the neck. And if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is strong, then make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave it so that the most of the thickness of the horn is burned, and lift your hand; afterwards, cure it until it is healed. This is the manner of the "olivare" cauterizer that we mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy (or seizures)
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization except for those who are afflicted with wind, and it is necessary to first purify the brain with juices and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is old and suffering from a strong disease.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer from it, then make gargling and mastication that purify the brain often with good meats; afterwards, wash the head in the middle, and I make one cauterization according to what we said before, and one cauterization on the vassel, and on each horn. And if the patient is strong and suffering, then make cauterizations as I said for someone who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and it will be the olive cauterizer according to the manner that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, then make one subtle cauterization in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and thick wind forms: then cauterize with many cauterizations as we said for someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities decline towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist: then give them drinkable things by which the brain may be purified, according to what is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After washing the head of the patient: then make one patch of linen well made, in the shape of a circle, which he puts on his head; and the patient should be crossed, and be well held from all sides. Then apply the liniment, and worth meads of old butter of thyme; and heat it moderately, so that the oil can be poured into it; afterwards, empty the patch by inside in the head, and let it cool down. And do this to the patient once a week with another good governance, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you wish to cauterize the skin, making several points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cauterization cools the brain equally; and then put on damp cotton in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	Of eye ache (or conjunctivitis)
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When eye ache comes first to the eyes by the signs that I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient drinkable things purifying the head, and beware of all moistures, and make him sweat or have a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, command him to wash his head, and make a cauterization inside the head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the descending of the eye ache is to both eyes together, or to one if it is to one; and scrape out all the veins and arteries that are under the skin, and let the cauterizer be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop with the same power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at incising the cautery how to stretch it out; and whenever you make a cautery or burn an instrument between the two bones below.
dou cors des larmes	From the depths of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from them are old and accustomed and are above the voice box, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and you see that they are cold, frothy superfluities, then he makes the cautery that I said at the beginning of the operation descending to the eyes: 1 cautery within the head, and 2 cauterizes above the 2 temples, and 2 cauterizes or burners below the 2 bones; and if it is necessary more, so that he cauterizes sagely over the crown on one little cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	From within the depths of the tears in the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit at all, then give him to drink 3 bitter almonds; afterwards bind on the head a cloth, and make a cautery with olive oil between the cauteries of the temples; and make 2 cauterizes of the cautery that is called "clavilis" above the eyebrows, one a little below the beard; and take care not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the membrane of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this iron cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	which takes this form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that it makes two cauterizations above the two eyelids just as long as the eyelashes are; and do not leave your hand there but for so long a time as the third part of the paper is burned, in the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	two hairs which point the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Whenever it happens that the hairs of the eyelids are turned into prickles and pierce the eye, and one makes cauterizations in two manners: namely by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or the fire cauterization commands the patient to let the hairs be as long and equal as they are, and if they pierce at their birth, then he binds them so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are equal, then the patient puts a bandage on his eye; after that he draws with the paper of the eyelids a figure like the leaf of the myrtle, and is the beginning of the sign near the hairs; then he puts moist cotton in egg glue and muskellee of persimmon on the eye, then heats the cauterization by which it has the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, cauterize above the figure you have drawn with a small point and a few pats so that the burn is red at the place; and the sign of the health of the eye is that you see the paper retract, and the hairs raised to the tip of the eye; then lift your hand and let it be for three days, then put moist cotton in butter until the scabbing is removed; after that cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs come and the paper is softened, then start again with the cauterization above the same place, just as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural height and is equal, and does not pierce the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauterization of burning medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs be as long and equal as they are, then make parchment the shape of the leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and hot mustard from each a third, and crush them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread on the shape that you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put on the paper of the eyelids; and if the disease is in one eye only, one should work with one, and also in both; and put cotton moistened in egg white under the eye; and the patient's eyelashes should be in a bandage and put your thumb showing above the medicine, and press one point and the rest all the times that the patient feels stinging from the medicine, because it stings as much as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine with your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blister has passed, then lift up the scab and look if you see the membrane lifted in the same way as if it had been lifted by the force of fire or by cutting; and if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply medicine again to the place where the medicine has no effect, until your work is equal and your eyes are in place; then put on damp cotton in a burrow until the scabs are gone, after that cure the place of the anointing which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to be careful with your work for great caution that the medicine does not harm the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft after that, and the hair pricks in the eye, then resume the medicine on that place which is softened with clean paper properly, just as you have done before; after that cure it until it is healed; and this is the form of the caldron of myrrh:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And you should know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and shape, and according to them will be your constraints; and do not show the right way to him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula, as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterize in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put his head in your hands; then bind him so that he does not move his head; after that soak cotton in egg white or persimmon juice and apply it over the eye; after that heat the cautery tool, and shape it like a goose quill, together with the handle of the cautery; if you wish to make it from one end of the head to the other, and if you wish, also like a tent; but in any case, this which is shaped is worth more for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula if it is open, and extract the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, work at it, and draw out the core; after that put on the hot cautery tip, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part near the eye so that your hands do not shake; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, so he must undergo the cautery again once, and another if needed, and let it be for 3 days; afterwards put on a moistened cotton ball in a burr, and the treatment of drying ointment until they are healed, and if 40 days pass without healing, put on corrosive ague medicine until the bone is exposed; and the king as it comes according to what he would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery of fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand, a fistula, and split the place; afterwards put in the split a subtle candle made of what this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they put in the quantity of an inch of cloth; and hold your hand or wick tightly, and do not let the patient move lest the cloth get loose; and it is necessary to put above the eye of the patient a moistened cotton swab on a spindle of eggshells or in an awl: the cloth will thus be at the place of the fistula, and the wound will heal marvellously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through the cautery that we said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, so it is necessary to administer a perforation to the navel, and bring the fistula back into its own place according to what is proper for itself.
des crevaices en levres	cracks on the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often times occur cracks in the lips that are called "pillicules", and similarly in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks in the way that we have said in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing iron according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it hastily into those cracks so that it becomes hot; afterwards, heal the place with cerote until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	Of a swelling in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When a swelling comes in the root of the throat or in the uvula or on the palate or at the roots of the teeth, and it becomes a festering sore and runs and becomes an abscess and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we said in sections, but it does not help: then you must have a cauterizing iron according to the size of the fistula. After that, insert or probe the fistula and hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the center of the sore and the bottom of it; and do this once or twice more. Then cure it as we said in cures, until it is healed. And if it is healed like this, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find written in your charterbook.
dou movement des dens	of tooth decay or gum disease (lit. "from the moving of the teeth")
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and that doesn't work, then put the sick person's head on your healthy one; afterwards heat the cauterizing iron so that the shape of it will come out in this way, as if you were putting a ring on the tooth. And put hot cautery inside hastily, and hold your hand until the sick person feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth. Then lift up your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will. Afterwards fill the sick person's mouth with salty ashes, and let them sit for an hour or two and rinse their mouth.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is congealed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupt moisture is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	of a toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When a toothache comes from cold or there is cold or wetness, and the treatments of medicine do not work, then it is necessary to cauterize in two ways: with a candle flame (cautere de burre) and with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautere of butter is done in this way: you take butter from a cow and put the end of it into an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a thread, moisten it with melted butter, and apply it hastily to the painful tooth, holding it until it cools down. And do this many times until its virtues reach the root of the tooth. If you see that wool and cotton are wet and cold in the melted butter, then apply them to the painful tooth, and put a hot iron on top until the fire reaches the crown of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The metal or iron cauterizer is prepared such that you take a dog of iron or bronze, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; after which heat the cauterizer, from which the shape will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer cools down; do this often, for the pain will be removed on the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the application of this cauterizer, and then quickly blows; and this is the shape of the cauterizer.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cauterization on whatever part of the head you want, and according to your ability; and this is the shape of the iron.
des scrophules	from swellings
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are of cold mucus and moisture, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cauterizer shaped from which this form comes later, and has two openings so that the fumes can exit to the other part; and place the hot cauterizer on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the depth of the abscess; and if the abscess is small put a cauterizer according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and place damp cotton in butter so that the scorching is removed; after which treat the area with ointments and poultices until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cauldron:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the humors overcome through the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first by soluble medicines; afterwards make a cauterization at the root of the throat, and take care that you do not come close to the throat, and let it burn only slightly more than an inch.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that make another cauterization at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and the cauterizer is called "clavicle" as we have shown before; and cure the place so as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	boiteuse
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	It seems you're still quoting from a medical text written in an old language, likely Middle French or Old French.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make a cauterization in piercing at all the cauterizer called "points" of which the form is shown before in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to thirty, or nearly so.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating according to what was said before, and there are three burns as per this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And therefore are the cauterizations more gentle, because you make three to the copper.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder joint is dislocated due to moisture and one puts it back in place but it cannot stay there, and it keeps coming out again with slight movement that has occurred, as we have experienced, then it is necessary that you reset the dislocation first.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards lay the patient on their back and chest; afterwards lift the key which is inside the titillate with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inwards, then heat up the cauterizer which has two doublets; this is the shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the key as far as it pierces to the chest, and bring out the figure of the cauterizer together with four cauterizers; and therefore the cauterization is made with the cauterizer which has three points, because the shape of the cauterization are six cauterizers; and they are the nerve according to the subtlety of a tent; this is the form of the cauterizer which has three points:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And on top of this one nerve, where there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards place on top of the cauterizer a poultice, moisten it with oil; afterwards let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, some thing will come out, then make a cauterization on the thick part of the burn wound, or many cauterizations in piercing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is reformed, and there is an absence of moisture, and the patient's injury is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold humors and much moisture come into the stomach, and they pull it away from its natural condition, and the patient has many cathartics, and in the usual ways of treatment he does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Then make three cauterizations one below the ribcage for as much space as a fist, at every cauterization with a pointed tip, and two cauterizations behind the two ribs so that the shape of the cauterizations is in three angles, and leave such space between one and the other that they will not be joined together when they become inflamed; and are the cauterizations so deep that they penetrate to the two parts of the liver, and the figure of the cauterizations according to this form without addition:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see someone being cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize him on piercing and marking above the stomach to a point according to the amount that you see from the needle; then cauterize him with all the cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the treatment that we had before, as long as he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes to feel pain from cold and moisture and from heavy windiness, as long as it is very much out of its natural complexion due to superfluities; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not help him, then it is necessary for the patient to be heated on his abdomen; and mark with a needle III cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this amount on the liver, outside the hypochondrium, there where the ribs of the man come; and have space between each cautery the size of an egg; and let the cauteries be as long as the body is, and do not press too much with your hand all over the cautery; and let it burn only the middle part of the flesh; and let the patient be straight on his feet; and if he cannot, then have him lie down, and extend his legs, and lift his arms.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your desire is, then cautery these cauterizations with a cutlery, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn too much of the flesh; for you would dry out all the body; and it should come just to boil, for the flesh is very subtle at that place, and you know this truly.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, they feel excessive pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure must be done with the mirrors, it is necessary that the patient be seated on his head; and then mark in advance the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterer which is similar to the sun, of which this is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with a cautery so that the kernels are burned, and come to the size of a small fig, until the ulcer is completely cleared; after the treatment according to the treatment of old ulcers until they are healed; and it is not necessary for this cautery to be used by any surgeon except one who has studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at least once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can dare to work with it, and I think that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cauterizer for pleurisy (an inflammation of the lining surrounding the lungs). This text appears to be a medieval medical recipe or treatment guide, likely written in Old French. The language and style are consistent with 14th-16th century manuscripts.
