Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from those wounds are descending over the face of the head and do not benefit from any medicine that is done there, and you see the face of the sick person becoming red and hot like fever; and the eyelids are tight and moist so that the hair of the eyebrows is down, and the eyebrows are scalded by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the old "cure for concussion", and you do this to the patient who has this disease: let them have hair on their forehead, then make three cuts or incisions in front of them equally according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions be as two needles' breadth all along in descending towards the nose, and the other two be at the temples by the papery skin, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are on the sides by the papery skin; and take your hand away from the continuation of the jawbones, and each wound is the length of three fingers across the joints; and you have prepared a piece of sponge and plenty of cloth to absorb the blood, then apply the spatulum with its two pointed ends as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is under the temple up to the second incision; and scrape out all the fat that is between the two cuts down to the skin that is on the bone; then make another part of the first incision up to the other second one, and then extract this poultice.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	and insert into the first cut the instrument called "culterelle", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side not sharp at all, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cut on the outer side of the scalded skin towards the flesh; and the inner cut towards the bone; and push it so that it comes to the main fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the stopping up of the ears.

de la gresle	hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow into the skin and cause inflammation, and they harm themselves, and bring about unpleasant ways of illness such as constant tears and softening of the papers and swellings, until it is a cause of destruction of the skin; and the treatment is in four manners: either by cauterizing together with fire, or by medicine that stings according to what is written before or in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done by incision and stitching or by threads, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should put the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper from the eye with your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, you should insert a needle into each thread on top and so that it is close to the edge of the paper where the hairs are growing, and pull up all the threads to the top of the paper, and turn it under the razor; then make an incision in the part underneath the paper, beneath the hairs that have grown together, cutting out all the scabby spots, from the large sore to the small one; then extract the thread, and put a small tent of cotton and fabric over the paper, then sew on top of the paper a figure like the calyx of a myrtle leaf, and in any case it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you see the paper rise which has been divided in two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if the wound needs to be closed with great quantity of paper according to how the paper is moistened; then fill the entire spatula up to the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large lower corner down to a little bit; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then place the wick into one of the two angles close to it, then scrape it all off; then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle all through fine wool thread, and bleed out the blood, and make the superfluity of the threads on the two rings all sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, then don't bother, then leave the stitches and the threads until three days or four; then treat the wound without stitches with things drying and constricting, for the paper comes alive at the union of the wound and its assembly but the stitch is dead (as the ancients said), and this work is without fear; and there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a shape like the leaves of myrtle, as we have counted, to three wicks cut off according to the form that is here
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then consider those who mount to equal strengths equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	If you are unable to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, take a needle with thread in it, and insert the end into the wound; and place one thread next to the large lip, and another thread next to the small one, and tie the threads together equally with your hands; then lift up your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have signed, as we have described, then sew together the two lips of the wound by suturing, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments calming it down; and sometimes the hairs on the paper are converted: you should use what we said about incision; but the suture in both cases is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of wounds is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two fine threads also long as the width of the paper and the space between them is; and consider the two ends of two parts where you hold the strings; then assemble one and the other finely on top of what rises from the paper of oil, and separate the two stitches from the two parts formwise; and let it be for some days, and the skin that has been separated will die, turn black, and fall off, until it peels itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time, if the wound has sufficient force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper is lifted, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two pads that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The stitches are made as follows: you take a fine needle and insert one thread of silk into it, then tie the ends together finely, making sure the length of the threads is about a hand's width. Then, in the same way, you order another thin thread of silk and tie the end of the thread; then place the patient's head on your healthy skin. And let it be in the sun so that the stitches are revealed, because this is a subtle and fine stitch. Then insert the needle into all the flesh at the root of the hair next to the wound, and make it pierce through the paper quickly as you pull it out from the natural hair. Then pull out the hair until it reaches up to the length of the stitches in the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the flesh is torn and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull out the stitches from underneath to all the thread that you have ordered, until the stitches come out through the small hole above and you can see them with your eye. Then you will pull out the stitches and the thread, close the eye, and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and grows back the flesh. And if the hairs are small, you will accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and raise it along with that which you have left, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the purging of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this sickness called "aleacrati" or the purtification comes into the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs from a sudden blow to an open wound or incision or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is that you cut open the wound and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen tents, and tie them until it heals; and it does not serve to use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the sickness will return worse than the first one; but it works with soothing things, such as fennel seeds; and rose of water or althea root and flaxseed cooked together, and an ointment made from dissolved gall-nut in any oil, and I wrap a tent around it, and cure it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you keep watch so it does not heal in its former shape; and these treatments that we have said are nothing other than precautions against this disease from returning in its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh (or tissue) that comes into the eye.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from a wound and a cut and a cautery and similar things; and the way of working in it is that you take a needle, in which there are two threads, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from left armpit as far as right, so that the thread comes out through two holes in the flesh; then sew the flesh above to the entire needle, and bind with a bandage not too tight.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper comes back as it should, that is good; but if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side inside the paper; and let the holes of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision that you have sewn, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape will be as the shape of a letter which is called "I griesche"; then remove the flesh from under the paper, according to the size of its edges, from what lies under the paper; then join the two separated parts and sew them with a linen thread; then do the treatment of what we have said about mollifying medicines and bandages until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	It seems like this text is describing a medieval medical treatment, likely from the 12th or 13th century. Here's my attempt to translate and interpret it:
dou soudement de la papiere	the suddenness of paper (or possibly "the speed" or "the swiftness") is unclear, as "papiere" could also mean paper or parchment, but here it may have a more figurative sense)
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness occurs in the same manner as paper is soaked with oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and hold it at tongs, just until you copy what is written in subtle ink that is neither too thick nor too fine, so that the patient cannot bear ink that is too thick to stain the eye; and your incision, from which you scrape this assembly, should be light so that the paper returns to its natural form; and thus heal the entire assembly, and make the eye clear of bitter salt, and wash it with sweet water, and eyepatch; then place a linen cloth between the paper and the eye, and put moist wool on the eye in abundance of egg whites; and after the third day, use the collyrium and things that soothe until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	The infection of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil. Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is such that the patient puts his head in a bandage, then the surgeon opens the eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coil the needle as pincers with double thread, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and put one hair of horse, or ox, or bull on it, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and drive it in between the nails, and pierce through the whole needle, and bind the nail with thread and stretch it upwards, and scrape off all the surrounding flesh from the costum of the nail that leads to the pulp and the skin up to the head, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the nail to all its subtle threads and small forces, and leave the natural flesh of the nail so that by the incision no tears come out as usual; and sometimes tie the nail with just the thread, and thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the surrounding soft skin from which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the nail bed does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the pulp is not pierced; and after the incision pour a little bit of thread silk into the eye, and from the suture made of litargyrium, and leave it until the next day; then cure it with what is needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you can't push the needle in, and the sutures can't enter, it has been cured many times with this kind of medicine; and they grow as I have said in the division; and if you see them growing, so work on the eye of the patient, and take a thin piece of skin from the root of the nail according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee. de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	It seems like we've transitioned from a medical context to a historical/linguistic one.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men's eyes have once been red and covered the iris and held steady on the pupils and turned towards the back, and seem like a mulberry rose; and the work is that the patient puts his head in vinegar, then he opens the eyes, and cuts out all that red flesh with suitable needles for this, and sustains it with force; then cut the first redness, and keep cutting to the razor until the end, and take care not to prick the eye during the operation; and let the incision be just like what we have said in the incision of the eyelid and in the small forces from which one removes the whitish part, as shown by the shape after this chapter; and when the incision is completed and all the red flesh has been removed, apply a drop of very red liquid medicine or similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and put cotton on the back of the eye with an egg white paste, so that it may be secure from hot abscess; and if nothing remains and the blood ceases to rise, and you doubt there is a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the hot abscess with soothing things for hot abscess; then return to your operation until it is healed, and thus make any red flesh that has been stuck in the eye by this likeness.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Mais il est nécessaire que tu apaises la cure de chaque œil faible par la voie naturelle, et de la voie accidentelle, avec des ouvrages de fer; et ne mette pas ta main dans aucun de ces ouvrages tant que tu ne vois pas que ce membre soit souffrant sous cet ouvrage.
des voines des eulz	Je pense que nous sommes revenus à la partie du texte qui parle spécifiquement des veines des yeux.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red welts are on the eye that are covered above it; they hinder the work of sight and weaken the eye forever.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary for the first that you look at whether the eye in which the red welts are has a white spot, and there is no other outer malady except the red welts; then bind it in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins up to all their length according to your knowledge, and be the needles thin double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two needles by degrees in one course according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then take the needles and gently force them into those veins, and check the bleeding every hour again until you see those external veins in the eye being removed; and be careful not to prick the oil with the sharp ends of the needles, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't miss those veins; and when you have done this, distill green and red vermillion into the eye to corrupt what remains in the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to remove all the blood in that one hour, make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it stay for several days until the pains have been alleviated and you are assured that an abscess has not formed, then resume doing this in the manner described above until it is healed. And this is the form of treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	It seems I was able to decipher some ancient medical text for you. The text appears to be describing a medical procedure for treating a condition known as "fistule de l'oil" or "eye fistula", which is a abnormal connection between the eye and another structure, such as a vein.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeons call them "arissati" fistules: when you treat it with a cautery and burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then it is necessary to cut into the abscess above where it should be dead, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see the corruption and blackness, then reshape it with all the instrument by which this form was created; and it is called an "aspre chief", and should be made of iron into a shape resembling a .i. (one) sharp point, and should be sharpened like a chisel so that it resembles the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is reduced; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal cauterizers.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the swelling is solidified and flesh has formed, and the body of the boil has solidified and remained like that for XL days, and it does not revive and is not inflamed, and no evil happens to it, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other cure than bringing the fistula back to the navel's pit according to this shape: and you uncover from the bone the second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered take a needle according to this shape, and be the iron of the needle at III angles, and the point be attenuated up to the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the armpit, and move your hand away from the eye. I poke, then turn to all the force until it pierces the bone and the patient feels through what the vein flows in if they hold their hand on their neck; and then restore the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the place, then send the material to the neck; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the pus of the eye.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens wide and there is no disturbance or reduction in sight, it's time to let the patient see again. Then dress the wound with a poultice made from acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then bandage the eye over with cloths and drapery. The manner of tying the drapery is this: take soft cloth and double each piece four times, and then place one on top of the other as needed for the size of the wound. Then tie it down with a sturdy bandage, and repeat the application of the poultice and drapery and the ventouses to suck out any remaining pus without causing further harm.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	A fall from a high place.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the tear comes in the conjunctival sac, it opens, and comes forth with threads like a drop of resin, and it is terrible to see; then if you close it, the stitches are such that you would put an awl into the root of the lower part, as far as up to the upper one, then put another awl where there is a double thread in the eye of the tear; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its position; then close the hole of the double thread and tie a part of the conjunctiva around, and tighten it well, then extract the awl and put on the oily linseed oil soaked in egg white; and let it stay until the thread sticks with the conjunctiva, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at any time the wound is tightened by the conjunctiva each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.

And if the eye seems to have a great appearance, then make it pierce with a very fine awl that comes into the depth of the eye, and repair the moistened albugo and descend the eye, and enter inside quickly; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Il semble que vous me donnez des extraits d'un texte ancien qui décrit des traitements pour les maladies oculaires.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not apart from the bowstring that is assembled in the eye, appearing like water flowing down, and it's not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands with two parts, and look until you see the bowstring come up to your eyes; then be sure, and do not descend and break the light, and see the things of the patient as he is used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bowstring is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Sit the patient between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and place it above the scar tissue on the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, so that the pus issues; and when it has issued, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or hot water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then be cured with another treatment until they are healed.
des aigues de l’oil	This text appears to be a medical term or description from an older language, likely Old French. Here's my attempt to translate it into English:
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the similarities of water in division, and what is necessary to pierce; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, far from light for the sun, and have the healthy eye closed very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if they are on the right; then take with your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or with your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then place the point of the instrument next to the cornea through a gap as large as a grain in that white part of the eye near the inner corner; then push the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand so it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel when almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the length of the path of almagda be as deep as the length of the diameter from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and that is the cornea of the eye; if you see bone in that paper for the clarity of the white part, and then place the instrument just to the point where the water is, then press it under a path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the waters descend now, the patient sees before him and has the instrument in his eye.

After rest for a little while, and if the waters rise again to the second part, put force with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not go up, gently extract it by turning your hand slowly and slowly; then put in the eye a thread of silk and lift the skin from inside.

Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are of our time, we place a poultice with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", about which I am going to tell you.

And then therefore prick the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deeply, but make it subtle, then put in as much as we have said; and upon completing the work prepare for the patient a suitable bed, on which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head to right or left, and let him lie according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and you must not do this now in the cure or after the incision, but rather delay it, because the waters rise quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess forms, instruct the patient to bind the eye in front of it on the seventh day, and to apply a poultice that soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, release the bandage and place a patch over its face for at least a year, and let it stay in that dark house.

And one came to us who was from the region of Yrach (a medieval name for Iraq or Persia), and he said that in his peaceful land, they used to perform almagda incision, by which they could cure the eye, but I have never seen anyone do this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in old books; and perhaps it is a new thing.

de la char sor le neis	Il semble que vous avez mentionné une partie du texte qui n'est pas directement liée à la traduction précédente.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises in the head of one who has suffered from it; it grows and becomes large eventually to the point where it is visible to look at; and therefore you must cut out the diseased part at the beginning, and burn the bone entirely, then apply the cautery or hot medicine on top of it; and if you delay cutting it out until it is large, take note whether it has become hard, dark in color, lacking sense: do not touch it with iron because that's a malignant abscess, for when you cut into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of pure appearance, not dark in color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, the patient feels empty and free from pain, and cures quickly of things constricting and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the diseased part is cut out and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes into one of these joint workings, it brings little profit, for in some men.

des apostemes des levres	swellings of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes at home swellings appear inside the lips which are hard, resembling grains of millet, small and large; then you must turn the lips back and split each one with a knife and take it to the pincers and cut into each part; then apply vinegar to the place after the incision, so that the swelling is dulled; and then let it dry out and cure the place with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the gum flesh
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often on the gums a tumor-like flesh appears, which the old call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with pincers and cut at its root and let blood or pus come out; then apply vinegar to the place or other drying and desiccative powders; and if that flesh comes back after the incision and often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: if it does not come back after cauterizing, those are the forms of tumors for cutting.
des sordens	of the ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the molars, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and greenish and wormy, until corruption comes to the gum, and it smells bad; then you need to have the patient sit in your hands, and his chin be on your saint (knee?), and remove the molars or scabs that show, as long as there's nothing left; and similarly do with the blackness, greenishness, yellowness, and other spots, until they are clean; and if you take out what was at the first cause, it's good; but if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the scrapers that are used to remove molars outside the teeth have different forms than those used to remove them between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you ready.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It's necessary when you cure a tooth from its pain that you don't rush to draw it out as soon as you can, because it shouldn't be done; for it's a very high substance, just so there should be no excuse for drawing it. (This text is talking about the importance of not removing a tooth too quickly or prematurely, likely in a dental procedure)
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to void, it becomes necessary for you to know the time of the stool.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient's pain deceives him and he thinks it is due to the tooth of Saint Anthony, and has the good tooth bled out; and notwithstanding the pain does not depart for that reason, as long as the bad humour remains, because we have already seen this with these saints; and when you are well certain of the time of the stool, it becomes necessary for you to scrape around the tooth on all sides in a spatula-shaped instrument made very sharp so as to ward off the gums from all sides; then move it with your fingers or fine forceps at the first touch and touch, until they are well separated, then hold the forceps tight; and the patient's eye should be between your knees, and you keep them steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and stick it inside from each side lightly, and move it just as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten into, you should fill it with cloth, in the place where the hole is; and if you have to pull out the tooth carefully with forceps, so that it does not break when being pulled; and you must work very skillfully around the gum for extracting the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and tell the patient that the pain will return from the root of the tooth worse than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act like the ignorant physician who by their haste and boldness break the tooth, and do not bring about what we have mentioned; but sometimes they cause great illness from the roots that remain or from breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with vinegar or ale and linen; and if it becomes bloody there, which often happens, fill the place with vitriol powder; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, by which one should extract the tooth first, should be long with pointed tips and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should have thick handles so that they do not bend when pulled, and should be well-made iron, and should have teeth to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains on the opposite side, you must put cotton moistened in butter there for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the place is softened, put in the pincers called "algefri", by which the head seems like a beak of a bird; and they are made inside like a file and this shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you uncover the whole char around the root, and then put the instrument called "althali", i.e. a file, which has this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through it, it's good; if not, use all the instruments, by which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And then one uses this instrument that has two horns, by which it has this shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other bandages which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems great pincers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is except that it cannot break; and know that many instruments of dens are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master skilled finds by himself his instrument, according to the works and the disease it shows him, for there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of them and such that it does not break a bone or the other bones, or it is possible, if he looks for the instruments which it needs, as I have told you, and helps from gestures, of what this shape is.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be big and well holding to hold the bone so it does not slip away but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place of medicines corresponding to those, and if there is in the bone putrefaction, and it is small, then reap all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural body, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly formed after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be shaved or filed: then file it; and if it is sharp with the tooth, take this instrument of which this shape is, and it resembles one small beak, and be of iron sharp at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to be filed, take the file with this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also done with the lime of which we make needles; and in sharpening the point of a tooth one should do so little by little over many days, so that it does not move until it becomes sharp; then polish at the end with no rasp at all, and if the teeth are too pointed and they hurt the tongue, you must whet the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth falls out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is knocked out by falling or striking, and the patient cannot press on it without spitting it out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, but this does not work; then they need to be restrained by a thread of gold, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold ones never do; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the width between the teeth; and if you see that the tooth is going in the wrong direction, take the thread and put it doubled between the two healthy teeth, then place the tooth between the new teeth, if there are one or more of them, until you get it safely up to the healthy tooth from the other side; then start covering again up to where you started, and strain your hand subtly and safely, as long as it does not move; and keep a finger on the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the threads of the string and tie them with a pair of tongs, and assemble them, and press them between the healthy tooth, and put it in such that it does not hurt the tongue; and then let him stay thus tight as long as he can remain, and if it loosens or the strings break, strain it with another thread; if it stays and serves thus for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the setting of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, such as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, if you put it back in place, fresh and fresh, just as we have said; and do not interfere with it unless one is wise and patient, and sometimes one makes a form of an ivory tooth, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Il semble que cette phrase soit une instruction pour faire une manipulation sur le fil d'or qui relie les deux dens.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this is the thing that comes from under the tongue or naturally, which one ties thus in place; or by accident of a wound that has healed; and the work is such as to open the mouth of the patient, and have their head against your healthy tooth, and lift up the tongue; then take the nervous string from the large one, so that the tongue is freed from its dwelling place, and if there is hardness or clot, and it's a healing wound, then put in the unguent and tie the string from the large one; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, then raise up the head with rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent; and let the patient spit each night, so that the clot does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is hemorrhaging from the blood, put vinegar on the wound; and if the blood flows, cauterize it with a slow fire cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the boil is red or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a carbuncle; and if it is declining towards the groin, and there is moisture, then pour out the unguent, and make a small spatula and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the blood goes to your work, so put vitriol powder on top until it dries up, then return to your work as long as you remove all the pus; then lift up the head of cold water and vinegar, and cure with other cures until it is sound.
des apostemes de la gorge	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! Les apostèmes de la gorge sont des ulcères ou des tumeurs qui se forment dans la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes a swelling comes in the throat which is called "godath", and it is properly called "the almonds"; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and yellow colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but let it be until it turns black, and then you will cut it out, or it would break on its own; and if it is of white speckled colour, and the root is fine, prepare the instrument to cut it, but first see if the abscess has cooled down and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his eyes be at ease, and he open his mouth and take hold of the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue underneath to all the tool, from which it takes its shape; and it is made of silver or subtle tin like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against this entire instrument, and you will see the abscess, then take the needle and stick it in the almond, and the thread should be above as much as your thumb; and remove any threads that are attached to the skin, then cut the abscess at the instrument, because of its shape, which resembles a claw; and though the tip is curved, one end to the other, and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	Je crois que je vois où ça va !
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cut from one side and the other named; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, warm water and vinegar, and as the bleeding stops, gargle the patient with water or cooked quince skins or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure them so long as they are sound; and sometimes tumors grow in the throat other than the two almonds, then cut them in the same way as the two almonds are incised.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born inside the throat, namely the abscess of little sense; and I had carefully closed all the throat so that the woman could not exhale because the conduit was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have been dead if she remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that I had to apply two poultices through the two openings of the birth (or wound).
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then at once, and inserted an onion in one of the openings, then the discharge flowed out, and I drew out a large portion of pus; then I reset the other part in the other opening of the birth, and I had him open his mouth and press his tongue; after which I inserted the onion into the abscess, and it bled just a little bit of blood; and thus was unclogged the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess continued to grow again, and filled up the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; at which point I ligatured it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus she remained without growth; and I departed from those parts, and knew only what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	Vous semblez avoir lu ce que j'avais traduit, mais vous voulez peut-être juste faire référence à "l'uvée", qui est la partie du pharynx où se trouve le sillon uvulaire (ou uvule), où se produit le son de la "r" et d'autres consonnes. C'est souvent au centre de cette zone que les tumeurs ou les apostèmes pouvaient se former, comme décrit dans le texte original.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the conjunctiva rises to the eyeball, and it is inflamed and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under a large and rounded one, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the boil abscess has been calmed down, and it is subtle, then you should cut it; and that one which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of a fiery colour or black, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger on the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is then necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I said, of its thickness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument which we have made remembrance of beforehand; then insert the spatula into the eye, and draw it back, and cut with the two instruments which I said in the incision of almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut off too much of the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut off more, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear from cutting, then you should use an instrument for the cauterization of their fearful sense.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauterization is sharp and sharp.

Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take camphor and yarrow and thyme and rosemary and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and gather them all together in one pot, and add a little water, and make it boil. Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.
