de l’aposteme des coions	A book of medieval medical text, specifically on "De Apostema Testiculorum", which translates to "Of the Abscess of the Testicles". The text appears to be written in an old French style and provides a description of how to diagnose and treat abscesses of the testicles.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this thread of sinew there is fear and more danger in many positions, for which it seems to me better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the procedure and the signs of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from within the body, and also from the testicles; and this is because of many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known by superfluity of bitter and yellow bile, which has spread to the testicles, or by percussion; and the colour of the abscess according to the colour of the body; and it does not find pain, and the abscess is serious; and possibly there are serious abscesses that are full of fear and pain, and of a mixed colour, and sometimes come from an inflamed artery, or an enlarged vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an inflamed artery, it is known by the warm abscess, when you press it with your fist; and it does not seem right that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from an enlarged vein is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fist, and it can be well done the incision on this resemblance, and on the other sinews; and that you cut the knot of the testicles, then let the egg rise up, and the string of the white scrotum, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hardened with its shell, then you should draw out the egg and the skin; and if it is hot in the syphilis or in those who are within the vials, then you should release all that impurity and the skin again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the abscess is at the back thereof, then it is necessary that you cut all around it and pull out the yolk, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your task is completed, apply the wound with damp wool in rose oil and wine, then dress it with other remedies until it is healed.

Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enclosed in a wrapping resembling a blister, with the softening of the scrotum, and the patient suffers greatly when he walks; and the cure for this disease is just as fearful as the previous one, and nevertheless we will tell you how to do it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier. Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	This text appears to be describing a medical condition where the skin of the scrotum becomes softened or weakened (amollis). It mentions that this can happen in some men due to the softening of the underlying tissues.
dou chastrement	The correction of a bruise.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is considered abominable in our law, and therefore it would please me if I did not speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two manners: one is that the barber know how to respond when asked about the disease and its cure; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, let us make the beast sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then taking them with your hand, hold them until they return to their normal state and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The punishment of tail-chopping: it is necessary that you anoint the beast, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie up the suspensory ligament, and cut over each opening to the sheath as far as the cutting; and leave no small sac or the delicate sac which is above the vasculature; and this manner of punishment is milder than that made by attraction, for at attraction there remains by chance something from the testicles, because of which the beast desires lust. Then heal the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	those with two sexes
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaudity is according to two manners in men: the one is that between the two testicles opens also like the shape of a woman's body, or it has hair, and sometimes flows out there the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has above the finger like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The cure for the swelling of the eye and the woman is that you cover the tightened skin all around, and treat it just like other wounds; in the second way, men from whose urine shoots out through the skin of the buttocks, have no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the hydra-like birthmark (tenta means "hydra" or "water-snake")
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a swollen skin closed over the natural part, as long as it is very ugly to see; and some women also have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you mark the superfluity of tentigene with your hand or a needle, and cover it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest there come forth streams of blood; then treat it with another treatment until it be healed; and a certain swelling comes up on the mouth of the genitals, and fills it, and perhaps bursts forth, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and for that reason they called it in ancient times "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you shave it, just as we have said to remove the scab, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	This appears to be a reference to a medical condition or a specific type of mark on the body, but I couldn't find a direct translation for "erratique" in English.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic skin is when the nature of the woman is not pierced, or the pustules are small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident due to disease that occurs; or it is due to a fatty tumor, or a subtle or thick boil, and it is made deep in the womb, or in the sides, or below, or anywhere; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly having flowers, and the knowledge of this is by looking at the vulva.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears close to the opening, it will show in your thighs or arse.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle boil and it appears close to the anus, be quick, and take care of it: put both hands together, and have the woman sit on her back, spread out her legs; then hold the two loins firmly, until the boil runs over, and the swelling goes away; then take wool, and soak it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman lie flat every day, so that she cannot break.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syphac is hard and thick, so it behooves you to let the cords come apart in the spatula-like shape of a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swellings are of flesh only, so suspend them to the armpit and let them come apart; and have bleeding medicines with bloodletting, such as dragon's blood, myrrh, aloes, together with a great amount of vinegar; then apply a broad bandage made of linen so that the wound cannot close; and thus it should be left long, and he should be given another cure until they are healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is a mass of flesh in the armpit, so it must be cut off in this manner, if it is not an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the enchantress's abscess which is in the armpit, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	from hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Cutaneous erysipelas are openings of veins from which blood spurts out without a cut; and when the erysipelas are old they become tubercular; and we have already spoken in the division of their likenesses, and signs, and I will say here those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and tubercular formations, when they are deeply rooted in the flesh, and do not appear by feeling, are not cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the flesh, which can be felt, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary therefore that you put the woman in a cold house, then burn the tubercular formation with tongs and cauterize its roots, then powder on restraining medicines of blood, such as theriac and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the bed for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is bleeding from these means, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomace peel and galls and similar things; and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and myrrh, and make into a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he holds still, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him have air-setons on the back and shoulders without piercing; then take linen, and wet it with juice of plantain or with juice of hawthorn in old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has rested, then treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a sharp head, so it must be covered as I said about the trephine; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Il s'agit d'un passage du texte qui semble traiter des abcès (apostèmes) qui se forment dans le rectum (marris). Voici une traduction et une interprétation plus précises :
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the groin, such as ulcers and septic abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the marrow, which is not one of the abscesses that swell and bulge; and if you want to know the operation of iron, see if the abscess is agitated at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then don't hurry to pierce it, but let the abscess grow and mature until the pain is alleviated; and then have the patient sit on a stool, and hold two small stools for them to lean against, and support their back and bring their legs apart from each other; and spread their thighs, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then push the instrument towards the right side, and introduce the tool used to work the opening of the marrow, whose form comes afterwards; and it is necessary that when you see the instrument being introduced, you insert the first needle so as to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and will not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt them; and it must put the cone of the instrument above, and mark the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess appears and it is treated with soft hand pressure, then it must be covered at the head, above the shoulder on the left side. And when the fist is empty, you should put moistened tented cloths in rose oil or green dried oil into the wound; place the outermost tent close to the root of the hair and place another one above the hair and on the armpit with a clean damp cloth in water or herbs cooked with meal. Then cure it after two days of anointing as is proper for those, until they are healed; and sometimes lift up the hair and the wound by washing with water and honey, and then with water or long-cooked roots of lilies and Aristolochia, and return to the anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is reunited in the marrow, then you must beware of cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Je m'excuse, mais il semble que le texte soit en français médiéval et que la traduction n'est pas nécessaire. Je vais donc continuer directement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs that are: when you see the woman hastening downwards, and desiring to smell the air; then the fetus rushes to come out quickly. Then you should know that this childbearing is according to the natural figure, and the issue comes under its head, and the second twin with it. And when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the fetus comes out soon. For when it goes up over its head, the second twin comes with it, and the mother is relieved of her superfluitities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because it happens sometimes above its feet, and comes out through the body or the head or the hands; or when it comes out onto the belly or buttocks, and is converted by chance over the neck, and in other bad forms. It is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures in which one must help it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fetus comes out above its head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth quickly, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a stool, or where women hold her; and bring her nature oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then put the midwife between her teeth the small spatula of this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	Split the secondine and cut to its angle until the moisture that is inside comes out; and press the belly of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek mixture in sesame oil; then make her bear down and cough with condiment, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands are too far in, then it is necessary that you withdraw them lightly little by little; and if they cannot enter, make the woman sit on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then let down the stool to the ground, and take hold of the woman, so that she does not move when she gives birth; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cut the hands with the knife that was put there before, and pull out the child, and withdraw it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the infant comes up onto its feet, it should be pushed upwards; and then turn it little by little until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps just to the hips, tell them to catch hold and make it cry with comfort; if it jump too far, may God want.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not in place as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to its natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be loose.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come too far as we have said, tell them to take muscadine of walnut, and oil of sassafras, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in warm broth up to the armpits; and when she is moistened below, apply the collar of myrrh and put it under, and let her be for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her cry and hold her mouth and nose, and touch her belly lightly, because now the infant jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child onto her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes in this form, so take hold of its feet and stretch them little by little; then bind it on its neck, and let its legs hang down, and be laid over the bed; and fold its feet little by little, and then take hold of its hands above, and remove the cushions below, until it is lowered down; and if the infant does not cry out, take its legs and stretch them out, then lift up its belly upwards, then take your hands; and take the child by the hands and fingers; and command the woman to take hold of herself as long as the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child which comes with a hand hanging down wide.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to help bring back the hand: if you cannot bring it back, then make the woman get up and go; if she cannot walk, then have her lie on the bed, and let her legs hang straight down; then administer the medicine that I told you about; and if she does not give birth, then have her sit on the stool, next try to bring back the hand; and take the child according to its natural shape, and have it cry out, and command her to hold herself until the infant comes out further.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its mother's neck, and has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards her back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the barber takes his hand, then turns him slowly and lightly, and when he is straight, sets on the natural oil of aloes and oil, as we have said, then commands her to move slowly; and when you will have done this, makes him sit on a stool, and commands him to hold it; and makes him stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	by the same manner for all the afterbirth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to the second stage in this manner, then cut the umbilical cord at your nail tip, so that the moisture is drained; and if the infant goes up on its face and neck, then cut the cord from the mouth, so that it is not retained, and the infant will die; then push the child inside, as much as you need to, and command the woman to hold herself once: then it will come out lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born at once; and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if they have no name; I know these, that they multiply, and are cut off by the force of childbirth which divides them, which is tied to the mouth; and sometimes come out also naturally like all others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut. Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For once it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes just to the bottom of the fundament, and is far from the body, then bind a poultice on it or on the fundament, and investigate those things.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the abscess and between two is the skin or the syphac or vessel, where it is close to bursting, if there are no signs of hope and faith except by the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it right down to the bottom, or if you can if you put tents and cure it in the same way first; and do not go too far in depth, lest you cut the lining which holds the foundation, and the discharges come involuntarily; then treat it, as we have said; by chance it will be cured, or you remove that covering and cleanse it after it has been cut next to the foundation, either with a tent or another instrument appointed for it; then cleanse that damaged vessel that is in the abscess, as long as you can; then attempt to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula away from the foundation: if it were an easier thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And at any time fistulas are made in this manner: and is when you thrust the tent peg into the fistula, and it is on the opposite side of the foundation near the skin above, so take a perforated tent peg at the top in this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I bind one twisted thread in two, and bind the tent to all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then draw out the thread from that perforated one, thus as you thrust your tent peg or foundation stake; and pull the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and let it be for a day or two; and then restrain it once again, so that the threads bind tightly between them, and bleed; then treat the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in every way that you can see, as long as it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make a hole that cuts so deep, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is sound.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spiny splint from which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cut into steps; and on the other side not at all, so that those things are not pierced which should not be pierced, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Tumors are according to two manners: or they are within the fundament, just like grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in the court also blood, and there is one or more, and are outside the fundament and at the chief of the fundament; but those who are outside so have little moisture, and immediately a small cup of citrine water or a small cup of blood, and have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them within the fundament, you instruct the patient to strain in order to drain into rooms, until the fundament comes out, and you see the roots; if you hasten, and hold it with pincers, or you hold it at your fingernail, then cut down its roots; and if the roots cannot be held because of their moistures, take them up by a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of kerchief; and extract them from your hands, then cut them, and powder over some warm powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, instruct the patient to take a purging enema and sharp for washing what is inside the fundament, so that it can come out clearly; when the patient strains, and if the thread comes out from the fundament, then the cure is light; and you do this by holding them at your fingernail or with pincers, and cutting them, then curing them as we have said, until they are healed, and it fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you sew the stitches in this manner: take a twisted thread, and insert it into an awl, and then pull the thread upwards and make the awl pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread towards the awl so that they are even and of good length; and strain the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and draw out the awl, and do this with all the others, and leave one for superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation a damp cloth moistened in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him be until he has slept, and when they are fallen, then heal them with ointment and other treatment, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when the wound of a devil or foundation (i.e., a dislocation)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often times happens a wound of the devil in the intestines, and through constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine doesn't help it.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape to the point of a splinter or at your nail the bark above, which does not let it moisten; then heal it as long as it becomes solid as it requires; and if it cannot become solid, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals thoroughly, and is scraped clean; then heal it as long as it is healed.
dou fremit	from a burn
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance that is found near the body, and it goes deeply into its interior; and often they find the frozen one, and people sense it just like a dead worm's tremor, and it comes in all of the body, but more in the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose pen, or a strong vulture's feather, and place that thread over the worm, until the red circles appear all around it; then turn your hand completely over the entire thread so that it goes deep into the worm, and pull out the worm from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, make a bandage of lead or iron according to this shape, and be subtle underneath and drawn above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that it does not bleed much, and do not press it hard. And if you see it, burn the burn with a hot iron, as before or with a cauterizer.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a catheter
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At any time made one catheter of silver or gold, or melted lead; and at any time made these instruments small and large, as they are furnished.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore which one furnishes in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small catheter and a large one is thus wide, or the abdomen is tied in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it has an abscess or the belly is constricted, just as you see, and the head is perforated from inside; and it has two holes on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is wrapped with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and is perforated all around with small holes, and there is an interval of one finger between each hole; then put in these holes a strong thread made of twisted wool yarn in X or in zigzag shape, and sew together the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if it ties up the instrument from the front with a strong thread, then administer an enema.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	The medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the blister with oil or egg yolk or something similar, then put it on lightly; then the attendants will squeeze the blister in both hands together until it is completely drained, then remove the blister, and raise the patient's legs to the level, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it drain as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps all night, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize him in a disease of purging the belly, and the medicine rushes to come out, then repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, then let the blister be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle blister above which the skin becomes strained:
des plaies	( new topic )
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will tell you of the cures for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse in accordance with how they are made, and in accordance with the places or the wounds are made, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are made by stumbling on a stone and by cuts from a sword and knife or lance or fist or arrow or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that strikes against the neck, or head, or chest, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because memory comes in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it's from a stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn apart and the wound is large, and you doubt a little of a hot abscess: so treat it right away with cephalic salve just in case there is bleeding from the wound, and the salve is applied contrary to the part that is hurt; and instruct the patient to drink vinegar and eat thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't heal, then let its meat be diminished, and not drink wine, nor chew meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come, a moistened cotton in rose oil alone, or in vinegar stiptic; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it's fresh with all its blood, and hasn't been moved by air, powder that I will say about later; and if the burn has changed it, then put on some ointments until it's healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by suturing, just as I will say about belly wounds, with suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered to the bone and can be held by only a thread, cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as cooked testicles and bread, as well as fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find an ulcer or corruption of the skin that is not at the bone, cut it all out and throw away the pus, then treat it; and if there is a vein in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped by medicine, tie off the artery, and if you can't untie it, tie it with a thread; and if that does no good, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if those wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that you put on this powder which heals quickly once the burn has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; and quicksilver three parts, and grind it finely, and apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then tie it well, and let it be without untying, if it does not swell; for you do not remove the medicine as long as it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make this powder of sulfur alone, if one doesn't have frankincense or dragon's blood, but only when the burn has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, just as it is, do not put any of this powder on it; but apply some digested ointments or a poultice made from barley flour and water and honey, until it discharges pus; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break of bone comes with the wound and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and is simple, then it doesn't have a difference between it and that of the skull, but if the jugular vein or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a boil, then there is no other remedy than to leave the cure and not put anything restraining on it, for it harms boils and causes them to shrink; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of boils is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be soothed by medicine such as salt water laved in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber laved also in sweet water, and other minerals in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is fully healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and high and full of pus, then pierce or lower the place; and if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then stop it, and close and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduit is kept in order by which the flesh goes, then cut the skin over the canal of the throat, but do not touch the throat itself, but put it back according to its natural shape; and then bind it gently, and leave it for some time, then cure with ointments that are dried until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then scrape it; and if there is fragments of bone, then take out all you can, and let what you cannot get leave so the wound festers, and becomes dry and closed the issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder over with the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula (abnormal connection between an organ or cavity and the skin), then treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of wounds from lances or knives.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from lance or knife, and the wound is deep, see if there is festering in the wound before the patient falls asleep: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on the wound at first hour nor bind it to stop the bleeding so the blood does not ooze out too far and go back to the heart and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor evil tremor of heart or estrangement from reason; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the patient with tentatives and other treatments until they are healed; and if they cannot heal, and function, then know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut of sword or knife and it's simple, in front, or worse, on the back, then treat the one that is in front first; if it's large, with stitching; and if it's small, with powder, and if it's pressed into the bone and has loose pieces, clean the wound, and lance the foreign bodies if they are unloosed; and if they aren't unloosed, let the wound rot, so that it will ease the extractions; and for other wounds on other limbs make a judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a ruptured belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the belly are great and medium and small; from the large wound there sometimes escapes some intestines, or the membranes of the intestines, by which their introduction is made; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it's worse for a small wound than a large one, so that we place the intestines in with pins, if they aren't put in hot to hot; because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they go in better with pins, and for this reason it's best for a medium-sized wound, so that we ream out the intestine to its place rather than to others. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners: the two common stitches occur on the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body and two other specific stitches are common with other wounds; and nevertheless they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines has escaped, and it is a simple thing to repair, this can be done in one of two ways: or because the wound is so small, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm him up in this way: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in hot water only, or cook in hot water with squinat and cypress and spike, and apply the intestine until the swelling is gone; and sometimes do this restraining, and be careful not to let it swell again.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with hot water or with herbs that are cooked, because by these means the wound can take in a small amount; and if it cannot enter, then make a small hole in the wound with an instrument used to lance boils; and the first treatment is to cauterize the area, which none of us should cut without there being great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: cut inside the curve and outside not, and look at its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, then put it back according to its natural form in its proper place, if you are able, for this is worth attempting.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is under the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head; and if it is under the belly, then place the head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly with a gut wound in one of the two halves, place your intention so that the part injured be higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to follow what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Place what you've prepared on the wound; then take between your hands the sewing thread which reaches all around the wound to its edge, and gather together the lips; and this is the common method of stitching, that you take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound's width, then leave at the head of the wound about two spans' length, and insert a needle where it has good strong thread; and pierce both sides of the skin with both needles of the sewing thread, which is inside the skin beneath, so that you make it perforate from that part, and gather together the two heads of the sewing thread in one bunch; then pull out a double thread around the needle of two parts, then gather together the two edges of the wound in good order, and then leave about two spans' length, and insert another needle; then tie the thread of the needle just as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this with needles until all the wound is closed; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and coarse, for fine needles pierce all through the flesh, and those too coarse cannot well enter: therefore they must be moderate; and it does not matter to thrust the needles too far into the flesh and skin, so that they do not pierce and open up the wound before the suturing; then remove the heads of the needles, lest they prick the patient at night, and put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles for a while to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sutured; and this method of stitching with needles is more advisable for small wounds, for one needle suffices here, or two; the second stitch is common, that you gather together the four sides of the skin and sewing thread bunch in one needle where it has a strong moderate thread; and when you have pierced these four sides all together, then remove the needle from the part where you began, just as people sew clothes; and place a space between each stitch the thickness of a small coin; this stitch is known to men, and I sewed up a wound that had been on a man's belly who was wounded by a knife, which wound was more than a palm in size, and had intestines well two palms in size, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned to him the intestines after he had been without them for twenty-four hours and the wound was sewn shut just fifteen days later, and I healed him, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he was dying, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal him with ointment, for I was in a place where there was none to be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean cotton on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle and stick it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced through straight in straight, then leave the head of the suture or stitch where you have stuck the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part to the outer part; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the tanner makes pelts, and leave a space once on one side, and pick it up on the other, until the sewing is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which the Greeks say properly, is such as any do, who assemble the two parts naturally together and apply one end of the silk to the other end; in this way: take a needle or end of thread nearby and make a hole only there, and leave the two ends of the silk; then turn the needle and make a hole from the outside part to the inside part as far as the two ends of the silk; then make a hole in one and the other from the outside part to the inside part as far as the two ends of thread on the other side; and this is the more proper manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this saying and some bear witness to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles or there is thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew veins; and know that when the rupture is within the belly, the suture is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the burn has changed it, so put back the intestine and the gut; then put on powdering char, and if the burn has changed it, put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and sew up the flesh, and cauterize the sifac, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, so put on, at once when it begins to heal, old cotton, and shake it II times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in many dispositions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will make community among the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten light linen with tempered hot oil or rose oil, and put it around the armpits, and under the shoulder blades; and if it feels pain or rotting in the bowels, and it happens many times, then purify them with black wine tede, and similarly if the rotting comes just to the intestine; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jun" cannot heal when they are hurt; and it is because of the thinness of the veins that they are in, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the proximity of its nature to the navel.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the splinter jumps out of the wound, then put it back as well as the intestines are, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, you must bind the part that is black so that there may not be bleeding from it, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the bandage, and hang the two bones hanging on the part under the wound as far as possible to ease the extraction when the splinter falls, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the great suffering of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people because I have seen a man wounded with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into an abscess, and from which there came purulence and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to refine it until he was healed, and the tear sutured.
