Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him being sewn up, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his belly; and there was no illness, but he stayed in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and certain experimentors said that when it has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take a fresh linen cloth from large looms, then gather the lips of the wound together, and when the cloth is over the mouth, put it on top of the two lips so that it holds its mouth shut; and then cut off the end of the cloth, and it will hold so that he cannot unfasten it, then put another linen strip in this manner as before, until the wound is completely covered.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That thread is sewn into the intestine and does no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a fine linen thread that has been cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread which is quite loose, and then tie to the head of this thread one fine linen thread twisted together, then insert the thread into the needle and sew up the intestine, and pull it through in a suture; and that way of sewing with thread has no other method except according to faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines' loops, there is neither remedy nor health, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it ulcerates, is called universally "fistula", and likewise when it swells and runs with pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the true nature of hard and white nodation without pain, and it swells like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes flows clear pus, and other times thick pus; sometimes much pus, and other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and above the skin, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is corrupted, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in treatment; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the propriety in the region is slow in digestion, and late in healing, and naturally inclined to putrefaction; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is fitting for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by handwork, or manual surgery.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Abcesses occur in all parts of the body; for they come to the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the scrotum, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and thus it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all abscesses of this manner are grievous to heal, and there is no other choice but to cut, and ignorance; and if there is any abscess that does not come just up to the place I said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know it, then take a tent made of lead or iron, if the abscess is straight, then search for it; and if the abscess is twisted, then search for it with a fine tent of cloth, because cloth folds around its twists; and if the abscess has many openings and you cannot well search for it with tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings, because moisture flows from one opening to another, and purifies it; then lance the abscess according to your power, as you know whether there is bone or nerve, and is quite deep inside, and ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when pressing your hand on it, and what place they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places I told you, then cut into it according to what I told you, and remove the putridity and the corrupt humors that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the abscess is very deep from a straight place, then you must cut all the way through, then I put moist tents in medicine paste, and pour them up to the head of the abscess, as long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then I put in ointments with healthy flesh, until they are healed; and if they are not healed by these means, then cauterize it just like we said, and if the bone is corrupted from the abscess, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not break or harm the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so that the king takes away all the corruption before, then heal with things extracted from living flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns to its former state, know that you are not yet gone far enough: pull out and scrape until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Know that if not, know that the corruption is too deep, so you cannot approach it; there is no other remedy than to let nature take its course; and if there is only a little corrupted bone, and you can draw it out with forceps, then draw it out with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, without leaving one behind; and if the moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, then chop and scrape the flesh and bone, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something caustic on the wound to rot around the bones, and let it be until the place is rotted around the bone; and then they will have broken down more easily; and if it's a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, so restore only the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then close the wound; and if there is great part of the corruption, and it comes just to the marrow of the bone; you must scrape and clean everything right up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was the young man around XXX years, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, so much so that the materials came to the leg and he became afflicted with a large abscess, and did not have any external cause to open it; but the physicians through their foolishness worked so hard on top of it that the abscess opened up and they let out a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and there came out many small holes which all flowed with pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians put treatment around II years, and there was no wise man in the art of healing, until I was called to him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what was flowing through the holes a lot of matter; and his body became red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent inside one of these cavities, and then searched all the cavities, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and cut into one of the cavities as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption had reached the inside bone; I took out what appeared from the corrupted bone, and believed there was no other corruption except what I removed; and began to restore the wound with usual medicines for a long time, but could not heal it; and then I re-commenced, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I took it out, and leaned over to stitch up the place; but I couldn't until I cut around a palm's length of the bone, and pulled it back to its whole shape, then restored it with medicines; and he was healed and stitched quickly, and there was no need to re-commence the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation blood would often flow, but he was entirely healed, and instead of the bone there grew a hard skin, and he was in good disposition and had no harm nor ill effect at all, neither to come nor to go.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it should be treated in this manner: take a linen cloth, and bind it to the head of the bone that is open, and have someone stretch it upwards; and put another cord of thicker linen than the first cord, and tie it above the skin which is over the bone, so that you pull the corrupt flesh below, and uncover the skin on the place where you wish to see, lest the saw cut the skin; and take a reed or a board under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and it must be treated as much as can be seen and felt the corruption, and it should be treated again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, so uncover all the flesh; then put embers underneath, and then draw out the corrosion from one part to another, and be the string as long as the length of the corruption I show you, such as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, so cut off the corrupted joint, and remove the bone where it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, so there is no other device than to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the elbow of the foot, so it is very strong that thing, but nonetheless you must inquire into that corrosion how it will open; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not oppose you; and know that the incisor and strings for cutting those bones are many, according to the seat of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare each instrument for every resemblance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so consider the instrument which you need according to what it will be necessary.
dou feu	with fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint can be damaged either from within or from outside; and when you have used medicine to treat that damage through the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then you must cover that member up to the place where the damage comes, so that the patient escapes death or the worse evil of the member's defect; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems burned by fire, and after the blackness, that corrosion of the member spreads from limb to limb, and takes hold all over the body; if you hurry to cover it up, and it is caused by the sting of some venomous beasts, like sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, then if the damage is at the head of the jaw, you must cut it off, and not give him a chance for it to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes as far as the hand, you cut off at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come as far as the arm; and if it comes to the arm, you cut off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it's death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue; and thus do you when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, you cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, you cut off the whole foot; and if it climbs up into the leg, you cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is that you bind it on top and bottom, and stretch one attendant's cord down, and another attendant's cord up, and you open up the flesh between the two cords a handspan wide, so that the bone is exposed; then you cut or sew, and put linen cloths from each side so that the sewing does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient other lesion and abscess quickly.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If bleeding from an incision occurs when you are operating, then cauterize the place immediately, or put some restraining powders on it; then come back to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to my father: he had an ulcer that seemed like embers of fire, and that ulcer came first in his toe so much that it consumed the whole foot; and when the man saw the ulcer, he hastened to cauterize the foot, and was cured; and a long time after, the ulcer returned to the foot of the hand, and he came to me, and I put him on things reflective after purifying the body, and the ulcer could not cease; and he vowed that I would cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of reflecting the material; and I also doubted that if I amputated his hand, that he would die, for the strength of the man was weak; and he completely despaired, and returned to his land, and hastened to cauterize his hand, and was cured; and I have told this story only so that it may be a warning to others who do it by necessity.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fatty place and remains for so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; and then they boil and break, and the pus bursts out, and the wound remains open like hollowed vessels; and the skin above is as thin as delicate fabric, and does not reach just to the bone or just to the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone deep inside, then it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is that you cut out that skin all around, and similarly when it is thin like fabric; and one does not wait for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is corrupting, and the corruption is not deep inside, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a castor oil purge thus: see if the breast is large, and the pus-filled hole within is foul-smelling, then purify the breast with Egyptian medicine made as follows: take assafoetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and put the mixture in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red and thick like honey; and then take from it according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and purge the breast with the medicine, and stop up the orifice; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then squeeze out; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and the pus is removed; and sometimes a purgative of ash-water is used when this medicine is not present, and it is to take ashes from grapevine wood, and pour water over them, then let it cool, and purge with it, as long as you know that the breast is well cleaned; and if the patient cannot suffer it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ash-water, then purify with water and honey or it has a small amount of litharge mixed in; or purify with honey and sweet wine so that the honey has cleansing properties and washing power, and the wine makes the pus heat up; and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well cleaned, then purify with what makes flesh grow within it, and it is to take diamantine ointment, and make it with rose oil and wine; or purify with some medicines and ointments, of whose properties I said the treatment of ointments; and if the hole in the breast is small, and the cannula of the purge cannot enter, then enlarge with a iron needle a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, as long as it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up so that only the place where the purging can enter remains open; and if the pus-filled hole that discharges pus is above, then cut or lower down to where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bow is in place, let no flesh grow; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you see it, arrange things so that the bow goes to its lowest position because when the bow is in place, let no flesh grow and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you see it, arrange things thus: so that the bow goes slightly downwards and lets nothing of the bow hang; and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast, and lay on top of a linen cloth that covers all the breast; then cut at the strongest point the pustule in the breast which is larger than the first, and anoint with soft ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the pustule, and put it on the pustule in the breast to loosen the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outside which once a week for many days; and that which is on the pustule in the breast, take off often so as to loosen the bow, and know what comes from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough or digestible or indigestible; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the pustule in the breast, then know that the breast is cured already, and approach health; and then release it in the morning, or the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the abscess continues to discharge foul pus after many days, know that the abscess is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons work slowly after a long time, you should not lose hope of recovery, for the patient is approaching health.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men who slowly recover their flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if bad digestion vomits gall from the stomach after many days, know that the health of the patient is not recovering; and if the breasts take a long time to heal and become swollen, mix dry medicines with moist substances and dry virtues like refined ointment, for it has a great deal of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take refined ointment, and make it with rose oil, and equal amounts of old wine in substance; then cook it and use it; and do the same with thickened honey when refined ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire; and then glue a cloth to it, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer long Aristolocha, and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour of vetches and centaury; and use simple or composite things: grind them, and make powder, and put it over the honey that I said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and made an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments; so treat it with the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the ulcer of the foot or ankle.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Pustulosis is an abscess that occurs under the fingernail or toenail of a hand or foot, or perhaps it occurs in other parts; and when it is grown old, and one does not take care of it, then the abscess becomes hard, runs, and discharges pus as long as they run to the root of the nail, and by chance they run all the way around; and comes the corrosion up to the bone, so that there comes a foul pain, and the joints of the toe are wide, and the color is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not benefit at all, then you must scrape off from it the entire superfluity that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to pierce and the wound becomes infected, then you must put hot oil under the nail that presses into the flesh, and let it rise up, and scrape off that tender flesh carefully and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines so as to remove all of it; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then scrape it and cut through to it, for as long as the corrupted bone is inside, it cannot heal; and if you see the corruption spreading, scrape it out according to what has been said before, then cure it until it heals; and if it is fierce, push it in, and it causes great pain, so it is necessary that you first lance it; then cut up the splinter of wood at an angle from above, cutting across, and beware that the saw does not reach down to the flesh which is under the splinter, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, place something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand;
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The swellings that arise in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy, and by chance there is a pit where there are bones, and sometimes a splinter, and sometimes they arise in the root of the joint, or the swelling is in certain joints.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with any defect of the thumb cannot move it, and he who is born with a joint in the thumb can move it by chance; the size of the one who is fat is light, in such a manner: cut into its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure, if you do not take care to cut it off.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born with or has an extra rear nail, it is necessary that you cut first around the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable thread for them, then sew until they are healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The numbness that comes to the fingers together comes by birth, or by the closing of a wound, or by scorching of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the scab, so that it may be repaired according to its natural form; then put between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or put between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is healed, as is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If numbness comes to any of his fingers with the palm, then cut out that numbness as it is necessary.
des vils	of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Swollen veins are large, inflamed pouches filled with melancholy superfluities that come on many members of the body; and there are more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary that you administer to them once purging of gall, and then cleanse with the oil of balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron [i.e. a cautery] is done in two ways: one where they cut them, and you drain the black blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein, and strip it all over.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting [of a vein] is done in this manner: first rise the leg with very hot water so that the thick blood is thinned out; then restrain the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide cut; then lift and drain the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the virtue of the patient can endure; and then tie it, and instruct him that he should dye of dark-colored foods; and restart the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and be harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s'il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d'aigue chaude tant qu'elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n'as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l'oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu'ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu'ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l'oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu'ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusque'a la seconde taille; puis l'estrai de taille en taille, tant qu'elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d'une part et d'autre, tant qu'il en isse; et garde qu'elle ne cope, car s'elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l'as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu'il soit sanez.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the eye is contracted and twisted and folded together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it diagonally, but do not cover it; and treat it in the manner that we have previously discussed.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one covers the eye is curved, and does not cut at all, so that it may cover the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were slender, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the limbs, in hot areas where no herbs or tree grows, and on land where there is little moisture; and by chance it may be elsewhere than in the limbs, and this occurs due to the corruption that comes from beneath the skin, as serpent and worm come within the body, located between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this inflammation are that it comes into the leg a very great redness, then the place changes and the inflammation begins to come out, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the boil bursts open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen cloth one and a half to two finger widths, and the wad, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it breaks open to the outside, then wrap around the cloth, and the wad; and if it is too long, then cut off part of it, and wrap up the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until it is all come out; for if you cut it, then it enters into the flesh, and brings an abscess and putridity to the place, and a bad disease; for this reason it is necessary that it be treated slowly and slowly until it comes to an end, and there remains nothing in the body; and sometimes this boil when it is treated two palms long, or ten, and one man came to me, from whom it issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, then it pours out pus or boils, and perforates as far as the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the matter which is inside is emptied, and medicines are applied to the place every day, until it cures like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at any time to this wound there are many veins, and indeed when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the leg, and a lot of pus comes out, and with it springs forth blood; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox", because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and the person feels it well when it moves from member to member, until it comes out through the skin where it goes, and bursts forth; and it is engendered by corruption of some humors, such as worms and serpents and lumbrics and ascarides in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drained, one cannot purge more than when it goes: so it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong string tightly; then cut on top and drain it out, and if the abscess is deep within the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire on top, until it boils; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or its head close to the eye, then bind tightly under it the sorcery spell, then cut on top, and drain it out; and the patient must be treated with cleansing of body medicines soluble for the bad humors that are born, and avoid foul-smelling foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windiness (or windy distemper)
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and it can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I looked again, and I saw it growing like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like fresh silver when it is cut from its place; the pain departed from that place, and lodged itself in the shoulder, and then it passed through the whole body, so that it came to the other arm; then she told me that it had been recurring around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease spread in that way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had often seen that severe pain was moving from one place to another, but I had never seen it like the woman's case; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and because of this the ventosity appeared constrained; and they did not appear in accordance with this reason among those who are healthy, and who have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to heal this sickness, and the patient feels that pain, as we have said, so tie above and below hastily, and then cut on top until the swelling is constrained to its place again; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, so cure it with those who suppress swellings, such as fetid pills, and scorpion pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those which have great points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and shafted ones; and those which have two angles, and those which have handles, and those with fragments; and the one that lodges in any limb so lodges in two ways: either in a principal member it pierces, such as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appear to you: if it is necessary that you take care of the extraction of this arrow, because many die afterwards in various dispositions; and when this evil sign do not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not very deep, then pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and the skull cap bursts which is on top of the brain, is when there is scotoma and swooning and convulsions and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of gall; and perhaps there are fluids from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps the patient loses speech and voice; and there is a moist white wound resembling boils, and it also bursts like a boil with pus; and if these signs appear to you, then beware of the cure, and pull out the arrow if it has not entered.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it lodges in the heart are that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrowhead moves like the hair on the head, and there is bleeding with a cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow when it strikes the navel is that foamy discharge bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the liver, it is near the small ribs; and there is great anguish and great pain, and sighing; and all the muscles of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps there is discharge from the wound of something undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly and there is a discharge of feces through the intestines, then there is no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine flows out and comes forth, and the sick person feels a very great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and wrists and knees and toes, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it's not venomous, as I will tell you that happened to me, for that reason.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An arrowhead lodged in the corner of an eye near its root: I attempted it and pulled it out from behind the ear fat and was healed without a single complication.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had lodged in the fat of an eye under the eyelid and under the skin, and the arrowhead was reset, and all I could grasp was the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was great from a Turkish bow, as light as iron without ears; the eye was healed, and no bad accident came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arabian arrow that had pierced his ears: I sawed off the barbs, and made it subtle as far as I could pull it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled out an arrow from a man who had it stuck in his belly, and thought he was dying; and then that he had passed XXX days, he didn't change his condition; I cut above the arrowhead, and wrapped it, and pulled it out further, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the arrow had fallen on the back of a man, and the wound above was closed up; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural condition, nor found any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was closed up; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and there are many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And take out an arrow from the king's man who was shot in the neck, which had begun to bend towards the right side; and the arrow was completely bent. I was called to treat him after it had been stuck there for 3 days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a fine needle and felt nothing; and he felt pain and discomfort below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I put on the wound an embrocation attractive and digestive, so that the area would not become swollen; and the shape of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the embrocation on again for many days, and the wound healed back up, and the patient remained so for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed medicine caustic on the wound by hand every day, until it was open and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrowhead which had become loose at its base; then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that medicine caustic, as long as the tip of the arrowhead became visible to me; and in four months it finished its term, and then it opened up so much that I put tongs on it, and pulled it out from one side and the other, but it could not come out; then I did not stop subtilizing and ingeniously devising with instruments, until I caught it one day with well-made tongs, according to the form that will appear at the end of this chapter, so that I took it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the sages judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your treatment on what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything; but wise masters are skilled at small things and on present and deficient things, they find true work, and new instruments, to treat unusual things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of members or are stuck in them except in two ways: either through the place where they enter or on the other side; and those that go out from where they entered are called arrows entering fleshy places, and sometimes it happens now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, then leave it until the flesh is rotten around it and the issue becomes apparent; and similarly if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for some days and move it each day; and then it comes out, and if it does not come out, then make a small incision all around it, so that the place around it is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the sides of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said before warn the patient: do not try to pull it out, but let it be until it is even after several days, because if the arrow comes as far as the skull's surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not reach as far as the skull, and the patient remains for several days without bad accidents, then let him try to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck in this way and cannot come out, then I administer herbs around, as I have told you, then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent; and if you feel it, try to pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then let the wound grow large; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has ears to which it holds, remove the flesh that is stuck in place for two parts up to where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can, until you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you would pull it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't pull it out in one go, then let it stay until the area around is rotten, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be opened up.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the hemorrhaging of blood makes you contrary, then administer what we have said about treatment in this chapter; and beware of incision on the nerve and vein, and devise how you can draw out the arrow without peril, soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest aid possible, and if you cannot, then put him according to what the sign indicates to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or if it pierces any part of him, or the skin is inflated in the area where one can see or feel distinctly: cut then above, so that the tongs can grasp it, and then pull it out: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, so that it enters into the bone, and enlarge the bone, and then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and start again the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is left in, fill the entire shaft with it; and if the shaft breaks, and you must administer treatment, administer the instrument pointed, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrow is lodged, place the instrument with the entering point inside to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is infected, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow strikes or falls on the back or belly or bladder or ribcage, and it is close, and you can cut over it, then cut there; and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew up the wound, as necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to remove arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look at this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and little ones, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, to stick at the tip of the arrow, as is this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and checking if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common body veins.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which one bleeds are XXXI, of which there is XVI on the head, to wit: two veins that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples apparent; and two veins that are in the corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and the two jugulars that are in the throat; and the two veins that are above the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.
