The veins from which one commonly draws blood are V in each arm: the one is cephalic and is located at the left costal area; and they call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "femoral", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right costal area; and they call it "vein of the belly"; and it is above the saphenous; and it is this one that is opened, which shows clearly on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and the foot are three veins: one is located under the bend of the left forearm, and the second is superficial which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "popliteal" that is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins underneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The purging of the veins which are behind the ears is helpful to the ancient cathartics and those who suffer from migraine; and the quality of the purger is such as I say, that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head: which you will take to be your duty, and where you feel the pulse under your elbow, sign this with ink; then take the lancet, and push it through the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand up all the way along the vein, and cut through both skin and vein in two places across, and make the blood flow out until you see; then bind and tie, so that it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood from the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is worth bleeding an old person, and a sicker one, and one accustomed to ophthalmia, and at the root of the tears sharp as eyes; and the quality of the bleeder so is as I say: and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and he feels the patch below your thumb, and then signs in from it; then lift up the key above the vein high on your index finger, and insert the lancet under, and lift up the vein high, and cut it, as you have done in the other two veins, and make a clot of the blood according to your need; then release the patient, and put your thumb over the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their clipping and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting from the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting from the celiac artery in ancient diseases of the face, and in migraine, and in jaundice; and the quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting, so that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and lift with your hand, or something else, and let two bloodlettings come out according to the quantity that you see; then untie the patient's neck, and tie the vein so it is sealed and at no time let the work be done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it does not seem right that the ligatures are too tight; and the vein is cut across, because the bone is close, and perhaps the ligature breaks when it becomes thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the two armpits is helpful to the eyes and to the scabies, and to jaundice, and to the cataract in the eye, and to diseases of the face; and the quality of their bloodletting is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting with some tie, as before; then let it bleed, and let the bloodletting be like the thickness of a thread, slightly long of the flame, slightly wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the ligatures are thin, perhaps they will break; then do what you must to stop the bleeding, and then tie on a layer of cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein so close to the nose is worth to treat fever, and to cure poison, and face diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the patient will wring his neck, then strain his nose with your left hand, and take the thin flame long, and stick it between the upper lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start to flow now; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then tie up the vein one night, for it is very soon restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two arteries so helps to tighten the spleen, and to stop bleeding, and many diseases, and atherosclerosis, and corrosion, and herpes, and boil-like things; and the quality of the blood is that the patient will wring his neck under both [veins], just as we have said; and let the master be on top of the patient's head, and the patient sit on the seat, then cut the vein of long a little wide, then extract the blood temperately, or as much as needed; then do it again in the other vein, then untie the tie, and hold both veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and let him be until morning, when the wound will be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the healing of books
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins of the upper lips helps against boils in the mouth, and against corruption of the gums, and cracks of the lips, and also around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of healing is to have the patient sit before you, and hold their chin as I said; then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the small dark lines around them: cut then both, and if you do not know them, and you have doubt, so cut the thicker of each side; and do likewise with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the healing under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The treatment under the tongue that helps after the treatment of the cephalic vein is for the constriction of the throat and illnesses of the eye and illnesses of the mouth; and the quality of the surgeon is that the patient holds between your hands before the sun, lifts up their tongue, and looks on each side a black vein: then cut both, but do not go too deep, because beneath them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck from which one commonly bleeds are healed in two ways: either they prick with a sharp fire point that is wide, or an olive-shaped instrument that is fine as cuttings, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the burning mint is very well-known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the large veins that are full of thick blood and apparent, and that contain thick blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the sharp olive-shaped fire point.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle in its pinching, and is for purifying the subtle veins, where there is a subtle, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are under the throat, and the neck, and the breast, and the belly; and it becomes necessary for the surgeon to bleed sharply, and to be wary of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and a flow of blood comes forth, then it becomes necessary to cauterize, as I said; and he must not prick with the fire point, but cut with the instrument called "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open obviously, you should drain it, and change another one; or you want some water from it, or you will let blood into the arm instead: it opens obviously; and the scab in the flame is dried out, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of the vein, it is necessary that you drain the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse; then mark the place where the end [of the vein] is, and then bind the arm, and dry the vein with flame and salve; and be careful not to prick in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: stop then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it coming out as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood of the artery: hasten then, and put your thumb on top for a long time, then take out your thumb if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it comes back, and medicine is not present to you, then strike the artery if it opens up, because the head of the vein retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a rind of fig tree bark and make it into a poultice, and take one half of it and bind well just up to the other end; if the flow is stayed, that's good; if not, cure with the powders which stay blood; and the staying of bleeding is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vinegar of the vein in wine is so effective that it treats blood from the head above and from the body below, for it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon to be careful for the nerve which is beneath, and if he pokes too deep, and he finds the nerve, and it swells up and the wound will be grievous, and perchance cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, then you must take out the instrument of anesthesia; and remove the nerve at your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The balm of the cephalic vein is so helpful that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and one must anoint with burning olive oil or with burning myrtle oil, for it is the most safe of all veins, for there are no nerves nor arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Always, it is necessary to seek the most gentle position, and not harm anything if one fails the first time, and one does again; and by chance the swelling appears in some men when one fails the first time, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the purging is according to your opinion. (This suggests that the text is acknowledging the limitations and variations in medical practices, and leaving room for individual interpretation.)
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about treating is that treatment is not done except to preserve health and to prevent diseases from coming; and the treatment must be done in one of the three veins which are in the throat: it is to say, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilic; and one must treat oneself at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears; and one must treat oneself on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who administers the medicine has no fixed hour determined for it, but rather as need is required day or night, in all hours and at all times; and one must not treat children until fourteen years of age, nor a woman carrying more than four weeks until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be purged.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be treated, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they loosen the intestines with a gentle enema, if they have much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw out superfluous things harmful to the main members; nor does one heal who is overly fat from meat, or drunk, until they are sober, nor those who are dropsical; and beware of treating after colic passion, vomiting, and belly decay, and repeated intercourse with a woman, and labor, waking, and jangling, and all that is not virtue, or by something of the arm or the body; then subtilize the humors, if the swelling is great, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you are able; then enter the bath, if no thing prevents it, to subtillate the blood, and heal from the belly wound around the third, as we have said; and guard that day of labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be joyful and jubilant, and let the healer be higher than he whom one heals, and rub the arm two times or three, then loosen the ligament above gently, for when it is too tight or too loose, it cannot cure the swelling; and then rub the healer's hand on the place where they want to heal, so that the veins swell, and one senses them; then moisten the healer's flame with a spoonful of old oil, then put their right hand on top of this wound below the place where one wants to heal, so that the wound does not burn and fail at piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flee just like strings to the surgeon, and those of such kind as are filled with windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retires from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if it overflows the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it behooves the surgeon to be aware in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein does not close the first time, it is good; and if not, then repeat again a little below that place or above hastily, if the swelling has not appeared.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is great, and the patient is frightened, let it be for a day or two, and do not bind up the arm: by chance there will come abscesses quickly; nor enter into hot water, then re-treat the wound if you please; and if the opening is small, cut with a slender knife and you doubt that it does not issue as much blood as you see, fire at the very same opening with all the flame directly; and do the work in haste, so that the swelling be great; for this has happened many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not reapply the poultice, and put on a little bit of linseed oil; for it lightens the body from blood, and is moist in that place the linen that the oil; and thus administer the linseed oil in each dressing that you dress the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and do the same with triacle and boar's fat, when put on the place; so soften the abscess and cause it to break apart when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if it comes to a large abscess, which has recurred many times, especially when the vein is not yet well healed at that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the place a wet sponge in hot water and vinegar for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding from the vein stops, and if it remains on the place for some days some blackness or greenish color appears, it will not harm him; and if you see something, put on some thing of aloes or myrrh dissolved in lemon juice, vinegar, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there has been purulent appearance at the site of purging from the basilic vein: therefore put your hand on it and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Be careful then that you do not put anything on it of what we have said, for perhaps there will be bleeding from the artery; but make one dry plaster to harden the place, and then apply another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And value each blood according to its quantity of virtue, and its color.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the blood is black, let it come out until it becomes red; and if you see a lot of it, let it come out until it thins out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the patient who is weak and feeble, and needs an extraction of blood, that one make a larger wound, and the flaps be wide; and for the patient who is frail, do the opposite, and he must heal quickly and often, and it should be healed by cutting across, not by piercing; and this manner of healing saves from hemorrhaging of blood and crushing of nerve, and is more useful than long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the patient to whom the body fails in healing, it is necessary to give a moist compress in apple juice; if he is hot-blooded, wash him three or four times with blood; and if he has a cold complexion, wash him ahead of time with a moist compress made in sweetened syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he vomits blood, after the issue of much blood, it is necessary that he drinks a broth of meat and a fragrant, subtle syrup, and uses the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and purge again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great purging, that he should purge little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to empty his arm again after the first purging, and he has a strong body, then he should purge 7 hours after the first purging, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if someone wants to be purified in another way, then they should be purged the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated up, and it brings on fever; thus you must draw out a large quantity, and enlarge the puncture so that it reaches to the heart; then, after you have observed all the conditions of purging, put your hand on his pulse when he is purging, so that death may not come in place of purging, and this happens many times, when the physician is negligent; and it does not need to be done, when you see the arm unbound, and blood issuing a second time, and the puncture is closed, that you press firmly upon it; nor if it is curved, let him stretch out his arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it until he purges a second time; or you put the point of the flame there, as long as the frozen blood issues forth from the vein's puncture, and put on a piece of silk dipped in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be left alone and do not bind it tightly, until the purulent swelling has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw out blood the second time, let him purge in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins on the arm are purged instead of those in the head, because they are composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of this surgery is that the patient puts his hand in hot water so that the blemish becomes red; then it should be bandaged moderately so that the vein appears well; then let the surgeon cut now through it, not wide nor long; and the opening should be large, and the incision should be sewn up close to the joint of the hand, and if any pus comes out, put the hand in hot water again, and leave the blood in the water until you have enough; and if this is summer, do not put the hand in hot water again, because it would be more frigid than in summer; and this incision for this vein is safer than all other veins, nor artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The incision of the salivary gland of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and it is the manner: strain the hand and put it in hot water until the vein is effaced, so that one can see it; and if the cut is made transversely, and you completely sever everything in one go, it hurts nothing; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are under all of them stripped of flesh; and then put the hand back in hot water, if the pus is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is necessary for you, then put oil and vinegar on the vein to close it up quickly, and do this with each of them.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purging in the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do exactly as I told you to do with the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The flesh of the scrofula is worth to all diseases that are under the skin, such as diseases of the neck, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its flesh is that the patient dunks their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it boils, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot many veins go out; therefore heal the one or the more spacious vein, or at the ankle, which is worth most.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you purify on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are under it, and purify diagonally also as if cutting; and have the flame very close.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water again, and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the remedy fails the first time, repeat it a second time above an inch, because the place is salty; nor doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus do with the scrofula of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee, and its purging is worth for the pain in the groin, when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The quality of his health is such that the patient should enter into the bath and wring out on top of the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then let him bleed in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and beware lest you close it, because the place is safe, and it has been proven to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then bleed any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and draw out so much blood as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put on linen and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of venesections
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made from horns, or copper, or glass; and leeching is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this venesection which is without cutting is done in two ways: or it is completely empty, or not empty; and the venesection which is made by cutting and drawing blood is done on 14 places of the body, because one is entirely behind the head; and another is in the neck; and two others are in the sides of the neck; and the ventouse under the chin; and the ventouse on the shoulders; and the ventouses on the hips; and the ventouses on the arms; and the ventouses on the legs; and the ventouses on the ankles; and venesection does not treat blood, except from small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it has not weakened anyone, as one makes a bath of vein; and it is not necessary to administer it, nor at all empty nor not empty, in any disease which comes from repletion, until the entire body be emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it happens that due to illness or by habit one needs to bleed, we should bring each person every hour in the beginning of the month or at the end and in between and in every season; for there are such people who when they have need to bleed, so have a heavy head; and those who find repletion and redness in their face and head and neck and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth and have swollen tongue and are bleeding; and there are those who swoon and see through the blood and are hurt and dying and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and likewise when it's in the middle of the month, let us order them to leech after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps against headache that comes to the eyes, and it does not need to be after the evacuation of all the body's blood; and this bleeding is instead of the cerebral bleed, and it does not need to be used by those who are of cold complexion or have catarrh, because it causes them great harm; and therefore old people should not use it, nor those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who purify themselves with it often become forgetful, and because of this it's good to place the leech a little lower by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind pipe swelling in the throat is a sign of the humour of the head and the spleen, and therefore it is worth its tightness at the constriction of the chest, and the bursting of the channel of the womb, and for all that, and also at filling; and you should push on it, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause choking or obstruction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind pipe swellings on the sides of the neck are a sign of the pains of the head, and dimness of sight and migraine, and at choking, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is a sign of the humour of the spleen; and you should command the surgeon to press his hand gently so that he does not compress the artery and let blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Leeching under the chin is good for mouth disease, and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it's in place of purging the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Leeching on the shoulders is good for disease that comes from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind pipe swellings of the sides are as worth as three veins of the arm, because they attract blood from these thick veins; and command the surgeon that he should not cut too deeply, because the place is bare of flesh, and lies under nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases underneath; and it's necessary that the leech be large and made of iron, so that it can bleed well; and if it were subtle, it would break through and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leeches on the legs clearly purify, because they draw blood from all the body; and are good for old pains in the hips, and in the loins, and in the bladder, and dispel inflammation; and are in place of the two saphena veins, and the two ankle veins, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause a feeling of lassitude in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the leech is to put it first empty, and let it suck immediately, and then place it hastily, and stir it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and appear the bloody juice; then take it off, and replace the leeches, and take note of the condition of the body, because there are some who have thick flesh, and clear pores: if so, it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to prick two times: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it's necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, it's sufficient to do so only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, then they recommend often; and if the blood is thick, then it should be pierced to its depth, and the ends so that the cups are punctured suddenly, and it is necessary for those with hard skin and strong, and who have large pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with dissolving oil: whether this is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucurbit seed oil; and if it's in winter, with nettle oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or oil of aniseed, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to whom one applies the cupping is with tender skin and large pores, then it is not necessary to put oil on them, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or morel water, or cucurbit water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very moist, should get up from the bed and wash with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive fluidities should rise with old wine, or with vinegar of their own juice, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or with similar things; and they should not be cured by cupping before the bath nor in the bath itself, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep afterwards, and it is necessary that they purge, when they should be cupped and when they are cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care of those who are sick with bilious temperament, and whose blood is too sharp and inflamed; it is necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in the ass, and similar things; and small onions, and kid meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, should take honey syrup and aromatic wine of medium age, which is between old and new, and small onions, and small onions and small birds and chickens; and the day that they will be cupped, they must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or muscat before or after cupping, in order to comfort the main members; and the blood should be thinned, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The poultices that are applied to cause pain are those that are placed on the liver and spleen and podagra and on the stomach and belly and loins and hip, for those members do not suffer to be cut thereon, and one does it only to draw blood from member to member, as we put them on the breasts when a child is ill; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put poultices on the stomach and belly to reduce the size of the member; and take away the pain, when there is an ulcer or stone, it takes away by its attractive virtue by chance the ulcer, or displaces the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts it on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness, and those poultices are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold tea, as in eye diseases, and in such a manner that one fills the poultice with hot water only, or with water in which herbs have been boiled that are suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the leech administered at fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And he must have two of them a palm and a half deep, and on the edge around the middle one small pit, just as to stab an awl, and it should be of brass, soft before so that it does not hurt the patient when putting on the member; and in the middle a rod of transverse brass or iron, to put a candle enclosed, and there are great and small ones according to the sicknesses and the age of those who take them; for the poultices of children are different from old people, and thin from fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must put this poultice on the member: take the candle of wax or the ointment, and put it inside the poultice in the middle of the rod which is inside the poultice, so that the brightness is at the bottom of the poultice that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the member, and it should be above the pit that we have said, so that when one wants to, if there is vapor, go away with it, and take off the poultice; and apply the ointment as before, and do it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered to patients with pleurisy at all times, there has no rod nor perforation, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member alone; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suction cups are not administered except in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in areas bare of flesh, such as the soles or heel, and others like them; and the quality of the patient is that when you find suckers that are in sweet clean water sense by bruising, then take them; and put one in sweet clean water, until they are sated and have nothing in their bellies; and then be bled from vein and cupping glass, then rub the member as long as it is red, and put on the suction cups; and when they are full, and will burst, if that place is where one can put a cupping glass, then put them, because it is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the place of ease, and then of sharpness, well enough, and then squeeze it; and if the place heals too late over the course of days, then soak a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the swelling is reduced; and if the swelling is multiple, then put vitriol paste or galls, and similar things, until it is reduced; or you put half a handful of green peas on the place, and leave them until they dry to the place, so now it will stop; and if you need more, then take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the poultices do not want to stick, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you put in a needle until the swelling comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are dripping, then sprinkle over a small amount of alum and linseed paste, or ash, so now they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	And here begins the book of cuts (or wounds).
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a treatment for cuts and ulcers.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear son, that foolish men look at this chapter, they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they read a letter about it; and for this reason is estranged the science in our land, because I never found any good ones; and I know nothing else, except by the science of the old books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and through experience, and through the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought forth, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the prologue of this book, which contains the summary of the words and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been proven to be wise can know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to someone, you must hasten to heal the patient from one part and from another, unless something prevents it, such as weakness of the body, infancy, or old age; or if the time is not very hot, or too cold; and if the patient has cold ague, that is to say, cold sweats, and meat of bird and goat, and does not drink wine, nor eat any greasy meats, and does not overfill themselves with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about a hot abscess or spreading matter in the member; then the patient will return to their original well-being.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you feed the patient with meats that make great nourishing, or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and cheese, and peas, and veal, and fish fresh, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with great nourishment, the muscles repair themselves more quickly and the break heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and the decrepit cannot be well reunited or soldered according to their nature due to the weakness of the members, nor those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but take no care, reset on the broken bone large splints that harden and join the member together, so long as they strengthen it as it was before; and do not leave him without his work, and for this it is necessary to nourish with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the thigh or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that split into a splinter, and others that cut in a sliver, such as the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with an open wound, and a break with a small crack throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each manner he must have his own tool and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remedy comes into its place; and it is known that the break of the bone by what the place is twisted, and opens well through the outside, and sounds under the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break; but it can well have a twist, or split, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It's not necessary that you move the limb with your hand, but put on medications that come next, and then constrain it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Know that the breakage that goes in a circle, and are the two parts of the joint, it is necessary to put them together evenly, so that abscesses do not form; and if abscesses form, let him rest for any day, until the abscess is calmed; then set it even with the movement that you can do lightly and wisely. And know that the restoration of this [joint] is more easy than the restoration of that which has pieces; then restrain, as it is necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is stretched by two parts, that is, hand or foot, or on your hand it is a small member, or on two strings, or with one string and on your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, then rejoin by all means the additions in their places with the movement that you can, and take care that through your work there does not come to the patient injury or pain; and join well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you should be able to feel it with your hand if it doesn't seem right: straighten it well, and don't strain it too much, nor press it as those who bring about warm putrefaction and contraction in the member do, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, then instruct the patient to keep it from moving, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and beware that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain; and take care that it be placed straightly, lest there come twisting when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in size, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as wrists and elbows and similar ones: then you must wrap them with soft and subtle linen cloth; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: then you must wrap them with a thick and strong string, for the wide strings encircle the whole great limb and bind it from all sides equally, so that there is no slack; then tie around light wraps, three turns or four according to the limb, and hold one end of the string in your hand tightly; then go above the break and bind more loosely, so that the break will be a little apart; and soften the string somewhat and somewhat, until you take up most of the sound part; then take another string, and tie it around again on top of the broken limb; then come back to the lower part of the break, and bind it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first lesson above; then put between the strings linen or cloth wraps, until they are all equal; then tie everything up with a bandage, and then place your splints well-made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or tumor, he puts on a soothing paste to calm the swelling and extract the abscess, and leaves it thus for some days; then applies a poultice with stars made of half of a large piece of linen soaked in vinegar, or wood like that used for making splints, or palm tree fibers, and according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the poultice cloth that he puts on the break is a little thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as it is needed for the member of small or large size; then holds on the poultices just like you did in the first treatment, then ties above a thread accordingly, just like was done in the first treatment on the break; the tighter it is, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I see in the works of fools who make their bandages with twisted flax threads, and this is a great error, because the treatment cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it is not necessary that there be less than two spans between each poultice.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the sick person is hurt by the scratches of the pads after being bound in their healthy areas, then put underneath them strips of linen or torn cloth to prevent it from bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is together with the break, and the skin is torn, I will say how to treat it later. (This seems to be a pause or a transition in the text, perhaps indicating that the description of the treatment for a specific type of injury is not yet complete.)
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it's not necessary to bind with pads all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Car when the member is great, it is not necessary to put this ointment too soon, except after five days or seven, or more according to your security from hot abscess supervening; and behold here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take flour which lies against the walls of the mill, and mix it with a great deal of egg, and put this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in many conditions, and especially for women and little children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and torsions: take 3 parts of barberry, danie (a type of plant), galbanum, asafoetida, and gum arabic, ana .x. Z.; myrrh and aloe, ana .v. Z.; aloes, 8 parts; and grind them into powder, and mix with a great deal of egg. If the complexion (color or temperament) of the person is hot, use this plaster, because it has good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is worth to many people.
