Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is worth for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, an equal amount of ten parts; myrrh and aloes, nine parts equal; aloe, six parts equal; Armenian balm ten parts equal, and grind well, and mix with water or a great deal of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plastering joints and bones which have come out of their places, and calming the pain ensuing; and they use the broken limb of a bone and the break: take new linen, and moisten it in ale and cooked oil, and place it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore [it], but they are good for calming a hot abscess, and properly ease the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones: take dry leaves of fig trees and leaves of wild pomegranate, and grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of a broken bone and to lessen the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vervain, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vinegar, from each one part; and pound, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix with moisted water of coriander or with water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of plastering more forceful than the first, when a hardened abscess comes to restoring the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and sainfoin, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; grind them, and mix with vinegar of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates writes that when restoring a broken member, one should only put on it wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be between two (temperatures) neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that when restoring a broken member, one should put on it dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is good for lesions and pain: take mugwort, the hair or wool of a depilated man (a person who has shaved their body hair), or bird's feathers, and wormwood, and equal parts, and grind them together, then make into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen the plaster a little afterwards, and take care if the patient feels no pain, or if the bone does not move back to its place, do not loosen it by force in three days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or inflammation, hasten, and loosen, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge from the sea moistened, and plunge into water, and lift up the limb, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased. Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, damp with water or rose oil, and bind it on a nut, as long as you are sure of warm abscess; and extinguish the inflammation of the limb, and have the pain removed, then start again the subtle binding, and a little plaster, and do not strain it so hard as before; and subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling have all been removed, and you still need to use plaster and bandage, then repeat it, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come to the member of what we have said, then do not remove it until after three days or four or five or seven; and let it rest for twenty days at times, as we see, so that the swelling subsides, and approaches the flesh on top; then restrain it even more than before, and its meat thickens, as I said before; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that there will be no swelling; therefore heat it with warm water to soften it, every time you remove it, and sprinkle a little salt in it; by this work the swelling is cut from the member, and mend it quickly what the foolish physicians do, who leave the member twisted: this is bad, and it is fearful work, and I see nothing else but to let go and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Il semble que nous avons terminé la discussion sur les plâtres et la restauration des os brisés.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of breakings, and various forms, and the causes are designated; for there are breakings that are caused by a blow of a sword, and the arm breaks all the bone up to the splinter that is under the bone, such as made by an axe or a club; and therefore this manner of breaking is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing it, and this kind of break is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two breaks is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a closed blow, or splitting, or a stone hammer, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is an impinging break, which approaches just to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has been closed in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and therefore this breaking is called "capillary"; and if the wound which is made either by being struck with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and makes the piece of the bone go inward, and it has an opening like that made by a blacksmith when they hammer up against the cauldrons; so enters the stone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to children who have soft bones, such as those of an infant; and it occurs in all these manners of breaking where small fragments are dislodged like those. And I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of breaks by the signs on them, and by the investigation made, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary break is recognized by this: when the bone has been uncovered and you rub your finger over it, if the break appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful for the bad accidents that come to the patient, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and swelling, and bruising, and high fever, and the skin is hot and red, and other similar symptoms in different dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any evil accident, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone in front of the 14th day at most that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the membrane under the bone does not become corrupted, and the accidents we have spoken of come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part in this way: and it is that you take hold of the head of the patient who was hurt, and uncover above the bone in every way that you can, and on the shape of the wound as soft as you can, and if the discharge of blood comes to reveal the bone, or a tumor forms, call for help from those who are required; and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest so long as the tumor cools down, and be sure of the stoppage of bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut on the narrow edge forward, and it is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another swelling larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various swellings, some are high and others wide, and they are sharp-edged, and of iron hardness; and work on them lightly, so as not to bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer swellings with awls, but not so deeply that they do penetrate outside the skullbone, and there should be a margin or a circle above the point, so as not to let the point pass beyond the bone; and you will need several, so that each one comes into place on the edge of the bone, so that you have awls for all skulls; and this is the shape of the three ways of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one awl on the bone and turn it back to your hand so long as you know that the bone is pierced; then place the awl elsewhere a little bit later, and do this all around, then file with the edges of the bones which are between the perforations, and make it finer than you can, and lightly, just as we have said, so that you draw the bone to your hand or to any of the instruments that you have such as pliers, pincers; and be sure not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, then it is necessary that you take out the splinter which remains from the bone with any other instrument similar to a file, but it must be more sharp and finer than another file; and if nothing of the small bones or scales remain, you lightly scrape them away with instruments; then heal the wound with stitches and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of doing it is that which Galen says, who is very wise; and I speak very strongly about it, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You need to describe the process of treating a certain type of injury.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, and the part is swollen in two directions, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer up, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and take good care of the tissue that is below; if it is adhered to the bone, then tap it lightly, because one taps off well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breakage does not penetrate all the way to the membrane, and the bone is scraped so only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to cover that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you must have different quantities of, in order to adjust according to the work and figure of the breakage.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you scrape with large rasps first, and then with finer ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other fine cutters and subtle breakages, it is necessary that you adjust according to its direction; and this is something that is not answered by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is open, then it is necessary that you take one cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten in rose oil, and put it over the wound; then take another doubled cloth in two or three, and moisten in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this as lightly as possible so that you do not irritate the abscess, then administer through it another bandage, and do not pull too hard until it holds the wound only; and let it be thus for a day or two, until the swelling of the abscess is eased, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and meal of vines, and powder of incense, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make into powder from these things, and put over the wound, and administer immediately soothing medicines without biting; and beware that the wound is soon clean, so that you do not leave ointment in it, nor let the edges assemble together, for when the edges of the scab assemble on the skin of the brain, they will rot and perish, and there will be great mischief to the patient; for when one puts over the abscess something biting, it festers above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil does not come out with the medicine that has been put on it, to the extent of its virtue, then you must take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix in one drop of treacle, and apply it to the sore; then treat it in the manner of treatments that is necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken or one separately, for they are two bones; and the part below is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it heals without being further inflamed or twisted.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you must push in your little finger or awl through the nose, and put this break even inside your index finger, and against the back of the head, until the bone returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and it cannot be brought back into place, then you should put it on top of a small reed, a little bit large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then redo it in this way, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has cooled down, then push back with the head of the nose a tent made of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you straighten it from the other side, if the break is there; and let the strips be so thick that they fill up the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said a certain physician that one must stuff the tents with mud, and moisten each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It doesn't seem right to me that they should be moistened with flour and egg, but it is necessary that they are moistened with the confection of egg yolk and mill dust; then let the tent dry until the bone is solidified and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes they bind on or to the nose a feather from a goose in place of strips, and if it has a soft drape that keeps the break in place, and blows gently through it, then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, then put in a plug of cerate or moistened cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a little bit of dragon's blood.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come out, then put on an ointment behind it, made of barley flour and frankincense dust, mixed with egg yolk; then put light torches on top and do not bind or tie the night; and if the break in the night is small, and it has broken into small pieces, then take it to suitable instruments for such a thing, then sew up the cut, and cure things that grow hard flesh and scars, and soldering, with ointments and salves suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the night, then let it be treated with poultices, and put poultices on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the distortion of the jawbone.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is distorted downward and there is no external wound or break, and the break is only visible from the inside, so that it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you place your index finger inside the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left side of the jawbone, then place your index finger from the right hand, and press the break inside slightly, and then hold it with the other hand outside and straighten.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is separated in three parts, it is necessary that you administer an extension of three parts, as long as it becomes straight.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth have caused displacement or distortion, tie one end of a thread of gold or silver or silk to each tooth, then place on the broken jaw salve and on top of it a double cloth; and on top of the cloth a well-made bandage or a piece of leather the same size as the jaw, long and wide, and tie it above the mouth that you can breathe, and command the patient to rest and take light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the face is changing, untie it on the third day, and then reapply what has changed; and apply a poultice with flour powder mixed with egg or fine wheat flour after removing the salve; and put a light linen cloth over it. If the poultice hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed, as many people have been healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses or swelling occur, administer what we have said before many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, treat the exposed piece of bone as dead, that is, do not take it as living tissue; rather be careful to remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it gradually with flames according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces [of the cautery], and there is no longer any of it remaining, if the wound is large, apply one of the ointments that are suitable for this, to dry out pus, until it heals.
de la forcele	with forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps broke several times in front of the shoulder, and the break is three different ways: either it is broken and split into two, with pieces, and this is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is this: when there is no open wound with the break, you should have two assistants, one of whom will hold the broken forceps in place; and the other will straighten out the arm towards the affected area. Then insert both ends of the break into your hands, so that it takes shape as it should, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch it further, place under the patient's shoulder a rounded stick of cloth or linen, and as thick as necessary; then extend and hold the forceps, and strain the stick in your hand, so that you insert both ends of the break into place as they should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you can't pull the head of the forceps out to the front because it's coming out from behind, then it's necessary for the patient to lie on their side and place a pillow under their shoulder; and have the assistants push down on the patient's shoulder, so that the bone of the forceps is elevated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find it is not properly aligned, it's necessary for you to split it open; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined together in any way, then cut it with one of the clippers that you have; but place the instrument under the forceps to protect the joint.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not cheese, and should be as wide as it fits, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has two joints, as you see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, such as the edge of the wound that you have made when you set the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, let the wound breathe, and if the incision is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloth and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then soak a piece of linen in rose oil and onion juice and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The strapping of the bone, when it is senseless from wounds and incisions, is that you put powder made from mill dust and egg white on the bone, and put light bandages over it, and place a spear under the strap, if you need one; then take a very wide cloth, three palms wide, then put double cloth over the bandages and the plaster; then take a thin strip of cloth, three inches wide and long, and wrap it around that cloth bundle so that the ends of the cloth hang down; and place the strip over the breakage, and turn the cloth bundle around the neck, and under the healthy shoulder, and under the sick shoulder; and tie each part separately, and when you see that the ligature holds the breakage properly, and you clearly see that the strip does not move on top of the broken bone, then reward it with something each day, and when the ligatures become loose, restrain them; and have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder, so that it raises the joint high; thus the break will lighten in strength by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it until bad events come, up to twenty days; then reapply the plaster if you see that it is necessary, and tighten it and leave it like that, until it is restored; and it is restored in as little as twenty-eight days, and less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	The shoulder break.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder breaks or its place is widened and you do not see that it is broken except by touch; if it heals according to the shape of the break and resets itself in its natural form, in all ways that you can, then put on the place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg white and lightweight bandages, and a double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle needle, a little more than the shoulder, and under the needle there are thorns in no part of the shoulder, so bind those hairs with linen cloths, so that the needle stays evenly; and then hold it all fast with a strong strip so that the needle does not move from its place, and inspect the binding every day; and each time it loosens, rebind it, and put the needle back in place if it has moved out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is healed in twenty days or in twenty-five, And when this number is fulfilled, then release it, and be sure, for it is not bone that sets itself in place easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone projects forward and touches under the skin, then make a cut up to it and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the boil to calm hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the boil
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, then it bends downward, and the patient feels great pain, lacks appetite, and quickly becomes nauseous, and possibly vomits blood, and the sinews are exposed in the broken bone, and they feel very ill.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and puts a pillow between their shoulders, then presses their shoulders, and gathers together the ribs of the two broken ribs with one's hands, and subtly makes it even in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is such as it should be; then puts poultices and bandages on top of the sterile cloth of salt, or another light wood, and wraps it up in one piece of cloth, and ties it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turns the tie around to the back, and tightens it gently, and rewards each hour with a loosening, and if it becomes too loose, then tightens it; and if it needs to be untied because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and scrape off the poultice, and address what has come there in ways of cures; then scrapes off the poultice, and tightens until it is sound.
de la brisure des costes	It seems like you're referencing a medieval medical text!
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not come from anywhere other than large bones behind the back, and within the head, and they do not bend outward only because they are slippery; and people sense this well when examining the vertebrae.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you place it equally across the break, as is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put a poultice on it, and bind it with an iron band, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib breakage is bent inward, the patient feels very great pain and puncture, as well as a sense of being pierced, because the bone pierces the flesh; and they feel sharp pains, are hot and vomit large quantities of blood, and this is a grave condition, and the ancients have devised great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, so as to drive the breakage outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot swellings come from it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then let them heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us said that one should apply cupping glasses on the spot to draw out pus strongly, and this seems like a good idea; however, there is doubt whether the cupping glass might attract unwanted fluids to the spot due to the weakness of its constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us said that the spot should be covered with wet wool soaked in hot oil, and a poultice placed between the ribs to put the warmth all around it, then it should be treated as one would treat pleurisy, with meat and medicines.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain because of the bone that sticks out through the skin, and there is doubt about it, then you must make an incision above the broken ribcage, and place something underneath to protect the spleen; and then you should cut into the bone, and draw it slightly, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and treat them with poultices until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, place a damp cloth in rose oil on top of it and on the place; and care for the place while the abscess is being treated, and let it be covered with linen or cloth over where it should be, until it is healed.

Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	None are born with a breakage of the neckbone and they become crippled because of it; and similarly to the spine of the back.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the breakage of the forearm (literally "of the breakage of the supporting arm").

And tie both hands with two strings, and lift them up, and have the patient sit on a stool; then place their broken arm onto the dowel, so that it comes to rest against the shoulder, and have a wooden crossbar in the middle of it, then lift onto some heavy thing or have the assistants hold it down below; then tie the restoration even with their hands together, so that the breakage returns as it should.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez. Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone has become dislocated, use splints, and put a larger and stronger splint on the break than the others, with a space of two inches between each splint, and so that each splint is as long as to pass three inches from either side of the break; then bind on the splints, in the way I said at the beginning of this chapter about the break, tighter and less spaced out.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", where one is small, and that is the one that touches the shoulder; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the small joint; perhaps only the large bone is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken altogether.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is only broken, then you must gently stretch and straighten it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, then you must strain it more firmly; and stretch it on the cushion, and bend the wrist of your hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others, and have the patient cross over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any movement; then extend the servant's arm to the part below his hand, or on the line, and another servant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the mirror equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, then put each in its place, and if there is one that is loose, grab it quickly, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we said before, and sew up the skin, with a thread of the same kind.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure. Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the treatment a hot abscess arises, then tie a cloth made from rose oil and white wax, not too hard or too soft; and bind the cloth gently on top until the hot abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax, and put on a plaster of flour powder with plenty of egg white; next apply the stars, and let the splint of the fracture be just stronger, and a little larger than the others; and know that it should have six or seven points in one or more positions: whether the break is in one bone, or two; and hold the break higher up than anywhere else, and always less far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths on the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the string holding it be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after some days.
